حصہ غیر معینہ ہوتا ہے جو حصص کثیرہ پر صادق آئین کا احتمال رکھتا ہے حاصل یہ کہ دلالہ مطلق على الافراد علی سبیل البدل ہوئی لا على سبيل الشمول والعام مخيص الا اور عام کی تخصیص بالقیاس تمہارے اور ہمارے درمیان متفق علیہ مسئلہ ہے یعنی یہ مسئلہ بالاتفاق تسلیم شدہ ہے کہ تخصیص عام بالقیاس ہو سکتی ہے فیجب ان یقید المطلق تو اس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ مطلق کو مقید کرنا بھی بالی اس تم احسان کے نزدیک صحیح ہو۔ فلجاب بمنع حواز التخصيص الخ تو اس نے جواب دیا کہ جمال مطلق على المقید ایسے نہیں جیسے تخصص عام ہوا کرتی ہے کیونکہ ہمارے نزدیک تخصص عام بسبب القياس علی الاطلاق نہیں ہے ۔ لان التخصيص بالقياس انما يجوز عند تا تخصیص عام بسبب القياس ہمارے نزدیک اس وقت جائز ہے جب اس
We transfer this qualification by qiyas to the expiation for an oath. And this qualification is a legal ruling because it is established by text, so its transfer by qiyas is permissible, and the negation is established incidentally, i.e., the non-acceptance of a non-believing slave is established incidentally, not intentionally. It is not that we intend to transfer this negation intentionally; rather, we intend to transfer the qualification intentionally, and along with it the transfer of negation will occur incidentally, and this is permissible in qiyas. So the author replied, saying: It cannot be transferred. He gave its reason: because the qualification, which is the qualification of faith in a believing slave, indicates the affirmation of the ruling in the qualified, and that ruling is that freeing a slave in which the qualification of faith exists suffices in the expiation for killing. And the negation of others — and in your view it indicates negation in others — i.e., the negation of the ruling in others than it. Its summary is that freeing a non-believing slave is not sufficient; it negates acceptance in a non-believing slave. So it is established that the qualification indicates these two matters. The first of the two matters, i.e., the acceptance of a believing slave, exists in the maqis (the case being analogized upon), i.e., the expiation for an oath, which you want to analogize to the expiation for killing. Indeed, the acceptance and sufficiency of freeing a believing slave is established by an absolute text, which is the word of Allah: 'freeing of a slave' in the expiation for an oath, because this slave is absolute, including both believing and non-believing. So by this absolute text, acceptance of a believing slave is established in the expiation for an oath, which in your view is the maqis. Thus, transferring this qualification to the maqis yields no benefit, because acceptance of a believing slave is already established by the absolute text. Then transferring it is nothing but obtaining what is already obtained, which is false. Nay, this transfer: now with this qualification you are only transferring the second matter, i.e., the negation of acceptance in a non-believing slave only. So transferring the qualification to the maqis is precisely the transfer of negation, and the transfer of negation is not valid, because it is neither a purport of the text nor a legal ruling. And even if we suppose, by assumption, that the transfer of the qualification is not exactly the transfer of negation, rather this transfer of negation is other than that, then still the main purpose of transferring the qualification is transferring negation, because acceptance of a believing slave is already known from the absolute text. Therefore, the former qualification cannot be the main purpose; rather, your purpose in essence is transferring negation. Hence, considering it an incidental transfer is not correct; rather it is an intentional transfer, which is not correct. Summary of this speech: The summary of this mentioned speech is that transferring the qualification is exactly transferring negation. If it is conceded that the meaning of transferring the qualification is different and other than the meaning of transferring negation, then still your main purpose from transferring the qualification is transferring negation. So his saying that 'we transfer the qualification and negation is only established incidentally, not intentionally' is invalid. Because it is known that establishing the negation is their main purpose, so this establishment of negation is intentional and essential, and it is neither a legal ruling nor a purport of the text. Therefore, qiyas is not valid because qiyas occurs in legal rulings, not in pure negations. So this transfer of qualification is being done to establish something that is not a legal ruling, i.e., the non-acceptance of a non-believing slave, because this is a pure negation, which is not a legal ruling. And it is an abrogation of a legal ruling because the absolute text that came regarding the expiation for an oath is absolute, and it indicates that in expiation for an oath, freeing an absolute slave, whether believing or non-believing, is sufficient. So by transferring this qualification of faith, this legal ruling would be abrogated. And how can one analogize with the coming of a text? Another proof of the invalidity of analogical transfer is: Among the conditions of qiyas is that there should be no text in the maqis that indicates the existence or non-existence of the analogous ruling. When there is an absolute text in this maqis, i.e., the expiation for an oath, which indicates that the qualified and unqualified are both sufficient, and there is no specific obligation for neither, then how can your qiyas be correct with the existence of a text in the maqis? Therefore this qiyas is corrupt. [The author continues:] And the carrying of the absolute upon the qualified for the specification of the general, as they claimed, is not permissible by qiyas. This is the answer, and it is a timing answer to this proof that Imam al-Razi presented in al-Mahsul regarding this matter: that carrying the absolute upon the qualified is permissible when qiyas requires it. And that proof is: The general's indication of individuals is superior to the absolute's indication of individuals, because the general's indication of individuals is intentional, since in its definition inclusion of individuals is included, while the absolute's indication of individuals is incidental, because the purpose of the absolute is either the essence itself or an unspecified portion that can apply to many individuals. The summary is that the absolute's indication of individuals is per substitution, not per inclusion. And specification of the general by qiyas is a matter agreed upon between you and us, i.e., this matter is conceded by consensus that specification of the general by qiyas is possible. Therefore, it necessarily follows that the absolute is qualified [by qiyas]. So it is established that qualifying the absolute is also correct in your view. Then he replied: By disallowing the specification of the general by qiyas in an absolute manner, etc. So he answered that carrying the absolute upon the qualified is not like the specification of the general, because in our view specification of the general by qiyas is not absolutely permissible.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute in which the author refutes the argument that a qualification (qayd) can be transferred from one ruling to another via qiyas (analogical reasoning). The specific case is the requirement of a believing slave (raqaba mu'mina) in the expiation for killing (kaffarat al-qatl) being transferred to the expiation for a broken oath (kaffarat al-yamin). The opponent asserts that since the qualification is a legal ruling established by text, transferring it by qiyas is valid, and the negation of acceptance of a non-believing slave follows incidentally. The author counters with several points: First, the absolute text in the Qur'an for kaffarat al-yamin (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:89: 'tahriru raqaba') does not specify faith, so acceptance of a believing slave is already covered; transferring the qualification would be superfluous (tahsil al-hasil). Second, transferring the qualification necessarily transfers the negation of acceptance for a non-believing slave, which is a pure negation ('adam asli), not a legal ruling, and qiyas operates only on legal rulings, not on negations. Third, the transfer would actually abrogate a legal ruling already established by the absolute text. Fourth, qiyas is invalid when a text exists in the maqis that indicates the ruling—here the absolute text indicates that any slave suffices. The author then addresses a related argument: that carrying the absolute (mutlaq) on the qualified (muqayyad) is permissible by qiyas, analogous to specifying the general ('amm). He refutes this by stating that specification of the general by qiyas is not absolutely accepted in the Hanafi school; rather, it is restricted. Thus, the attempt to analogize the transfer of the qualification fails on multiple grounds, demonstrating the limits of qiyas when dealing with absolute texts and pure negations.

Key Terms
قيد (qayd): A qualification or restriction attached to a ruling, e.g., the condition of faith in the slave for expiation.
تعدية (ta'diya): Transferring a ruling or qualification from one case (asl) to another (far') via qiyas.
عدم ('adam): Negation or absence of a legal ruling, e.g., non-acceptance of a non-believing slave. In usul, 'adam is not a hukm shar'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi author reject transferring the qualification of faith (iman) from kaffarat al-qatl to kaffarat al-yamin by qiyas?
A) Because kaffarat al-yamin is a different type of expiation.
B) Because the absolute text in kaffarat al-yamin already covers both believing and non-believing slaves, making the transfer superfluous.
C) Because qiyas is not allowed in cases of expiation.
D) Because the qualification of faith is not a legal ruling.

Key Takeaway
A qualification cannot be transferred by qiyas if the absolute text already covers the qualified case, or if the transfer necessarily implies a pure negation, or if a text exists in the maqis.

Why Qiyas Cannot Restrict an Absolute Text
Refuting the validity of qiyas in restricting the absolute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument that qiyas is invalid for restricting a mutlaq text when a nass exists in the maqis, and apply this condition to identify when qiyas is impermissible.

Core Idea
Qiyas cannot override a nass: restriction of the absolute requires a text, not analogy.

In this passage, the commentator refutes an opponent who claims that a restriction (qayd) from a muqayyad text can be extended via qiyas to an absolute text. The Hanafi position holds that such extension is invalid because it either proves a primary non-existence (not a shari ruling) or it contradicts an existing nass. We will dissect the two-pronged argument and understand why the Hanafi school prioritizes textual authority over analogical reasoning in this context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The issue is whether qiyas can be used to impose a condition (like requiring a believing slave) onto an absolute text (like 'free a slave' in kaffarat al-yamin) based on a muqayyad text from a different context (kaffarat al-qatl).
The opposing view is attributed to Imam al-Razi and the Shafi'i school.
2
Understand the first Hanafi argument: ta'diyah al-qaid is ta'diyah al-'adam
The commentator argues that extending the restriction (e.g., requiring belief) is actually extending non-existence (negating the permissibility of a disbelieving slave). This non-existence is a primary non-existence ('adam asli), which is not a shari ruling, and qiyas only operates on shari rulings.
See key term 'adam asli.
3
Understand the second Hanafi argument: existence of a nass in the maqis
A condition of valid qiyas is that no text exists in the maqis (the case being analogized) that provides a ruling. Here, the absolute text on kaffarat al-yamin explicitly allows any slave, so there is a nass. Thus qiyas is corrupt.
This is a dalil naqli argument.
4
Contrast with the opponent's reasoning
The opponent analogizes taqyid al-mutlaq to takhsis al-amm, which some allow by qiyas. The Hanafi response is that takhsis al-amm by qiyas is only valid after the 'amm has been specified by a qati' dalil; here the qayd is being introduced initially by qiyas.
Thamarah al-khilaf: In Hanafi fiqh, any slave suffices for kaffarat al-yamin; in Shafi'i, only a believing slave would be accepted if qiyas were applied.
5
Apply the condition to a new scenario
Given another pair of absolute and qualified texts, check if there is a nass in the maqis. If yes, qiyas is invalid; if no, qiyas may be considered (subject to other conditions).
This step consolidates the rule.

حاصل هذا الكلام اس کلام مذکور کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تعدیہ قید یعینیہ تعدیہ عدم ہے اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ تعدیہ قید کا مفہوم مغایر اور غیر ہے تعدیہ عدم کے مفہوم کا تو پھر بھی تعدیہ قید سے تمہارا مقصود اصلی تعدیہ عدم ہے فتقدية العدم مقصورة من تعديد القيد فيطل قولہ تو ان کی قول باطل ہو گیا کہ ہم تعدیہ قید کرتے ہیں اور عدم صرف ضمنا ثابت ہو گا لا قصدا کیونکر بل العلم یثبت تصد عدم کا اثبات ان کا مقصود اصلی ہے لہذا یہ اثبات عدم بالقصد و بالذات ہے اور یہ نہ حکم شرعی ہے نہ مدلول نص فلا یصح القیاس کیونکہ قیاس احکام شرعیہ میں ہوا کرتا ہے اعدام اصیلہ میں نہیں فتکون کس یہ تعد یہ قید ایسی چیز کے اثبات کے لئے کیا جارہا ہے جو حکم شرعی نہیں ہے۔ یعنی عدم اجزاء الرقبة الکافر کیونکہ یہ عدم اصلی ہے جو حکم شرعی نہیں ہوا کرتا وابطال الحكم الشرعی اور یہ تعدیہ قید در حقیقت حکم شرعی کا ابطال ہے چونکہ نص مطلق جو کفارہ مین میں وارد ہے وہ مطلق ہے اور وہ دال ہے کہ کفارہ ہمیں میں مطلق رقیہ خواہ مؤمنہ ہو یا کافرہ کا ازاد کرنا کافی ہے تو اس قید مؤمنہ کی تعدیہ سے یہ حکم شریعی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ وكيف يقاس مع ورود النص بہ تعدیہ بالقیاس کے فاسد ہونے کی ایک اور دلیل ہے . حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ قیاس کے شرائط میں سے ایک شرط یہ ہے کہ مقیس میں کوئی ایسی نص موجود نہ ہو جو حکم معدنی کے وجود یا اس کے عدم پر دال ہو جب اس مقیس میں یعنی کفارہ یمین میں نص مطلق وارد ہے جو دال ہے کہ مقید اور غیر مقید کفارہ یمین میں کافی ہے کسی ایک کا وجوب علی التعیین نہیں ہے تو آپ کا قیاس مع ورود النص في المقیس کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے لہذا یہ قیاس فاسد ہے۔
Summary of this statement: The extension/ta'diyah of the restriction is essentially the extension of non-existence. Even if it is conceded that the meaning of ta'diyah of the restriction is different from the meaning of ta'diyah of non-existence, still your primary intent from ta'diyah of the restriction is ta'diyah of non-existence. Thus the restriction of non-existence is subsumed under the restriction of the restriction, so his statement is invalid that 'we extend the restriction and non-existence is only established implicitly, not primarily'. How so? Rather, knowledge establishes that the proof of non-existence is their primary intent. Hence this proof of non-existence is intentional and essential, and it is neither a shari ruling nor a textual import, so qiyas is not valid because qiyas operates in shari rulings, not in primary non-existences. So this ta'diyah of the restriction is being done to prove something that is not a shari ruling, i.e., the non-existence of the permissibility of an unfree slave, because this is a primary non-existence which is not a shari ruling. And it is the nullification of a shari ruling because the absolute text that came regarding expiation is absolute and indicates that in expiation, freeing an absolute slave, whether believing or disbelieving, is sufficient. So by extending this restriction of belief, this shari ruling is nullified. And how can qiyas be performed when there is a text upon it? That is another proof of the corruption of qiyas. Its summary: Among the conditions of qiyas is that there should be no text in the maqis that indicates the existence or non-existence of the ma'dul ruling. When in this maqis, i.e., expiation of oath, an absolute text has come that indicates that restricted and unrestricted are sufficient in expiation of oath, and there is no obligation of either specifically, then how can your qiyas be valid despite the existence of a text in the maqis? Therefore this qiyas is corrupt.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent's argument that restricting an absolute term by qiyas is valid. The commentator argues that the opponent's extension of the restriction (e.g., requiring a believing slave in expiation of oath) is actually an extension of non-existence (i.e., negating the permissibility of a disbelieving slave). This non-existence is not a shari ruling but a logical inference, and qiyas only applies to shari rulings. Moreover, the absolute text (Quran or hadith) itself allows any slave, so adding the condition of belief by qiyas would nullify that shari ruling. Additionally, a condition of qiyas is that there be no text in the maqis that rules on the issue; here the absolute text exists, so qiyas is invalid. This is a classic Hanafi usul argument against using qiyas to restrict a mutlaq when a nass is already present.

Key Terms
تعدیة القید (ta'diyah al-qaid): Extending a restriction (qayd) from one context to another, i.e., applying a condition from a muqayyad text to a mutlaq text via reasoning.
عدم اصلی (adam asli): Original non-existence; a state that is not a shari' ruling but a basic absence of a legal attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because qiyas only applies to acts of worship.
B) Because there is an absolute nass in the maqis that already provides the ruling.
C) Because the restriction is about belief, which is not subject to qiyas.
D) Because the muqayyad text is from a different surah.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas cannot restrict a mutlaq text when a nass exists in the maqis, as the nass overrides analogical reasoning.

Inherent vs. External Restrictions on the Absolute
Explaining the difference between expiations and why the condition of safety is derived from the absolute itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a restriction inherent in the absolute term (e.g., physical soundness) and an external restriction added by qiyas, and apply this distinction to evaluate arguments about conditions in expiations.

Core Idea
An absolute term excludes deficient individuals by definition; requiring faith is an external addition needing proof.

This passage from Al-Tawzih wa al-Talwih addresses a sophisticated objection: if Hanafis restrict the absolute slave in expiation to one free from defects, why can't they accept the condition of faith? The author explains the difference: the condition of safety is inherent in the term 'slave,' while faith is an external addition. Furthermore, even if one tried to analogize from the expiation for murder (which requires a believing slave), the severity of murder prevents analogizing to lesser sins. This lesson unpacks the dual argument: the linguistic principle and the obstacle of qiyas based on crime severity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two obstacles to qiyas mentioned
The first obstacle is the existence of a specific text (nass) in the maqis (original ruling). The second obstacle is that murder is a grave sin, so its expiation's severity (requiring a believing slave) cannot be extended to lesser sins by qiyas.
2
Understand the objection against the Hanafis
Critics argue: Hanafis themselves restrict the absolute slave by requiring physical soundness. If that is allowed, why can't they also require faith? This challenges the consistency of the Hanafi position.
The objection is presented in al-Mahsul by Imam al-Razi.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: the inherent meaning of 'slave'
The absolute term 'slave' (raqabah) by default refers to a perfect individual capable of the intended benefit (e.g., work). A blind or maimed slave is deficient in the essence of slavery, so the absolute excludes him naturally. This is based on the principle 'al-mutlaq yanṣarifu ilā al-kāmil'.
4
Contrast with the condition of faith
Faith is not part of the lexical meaning of 'slave'. Requiring it would be an external addition (qiyas), which is impermissible when a text exists. The text (Quran 58:3, for oath expiation) says 'slave' without qualification, so adding faith would be a restriction by qiyas, which is forbidden when the absolute is established.
Thus the Hanafi position is consistent: safety is inherent, faith is external.
5
Apply the principle to the analogy of water
The author gives the example: 'ma' mutlaq' (absolute water) does not include rosewater, because rosewater has an added property. Similarly, a slave missing major benefits (sight, hands, legs) is not included in the absolute term 'slave'.
This clarifies that excluding deficient slaves is not a restriction but a proper understanding of the term's scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قام الفرق بين الكفارات جب یہ حکم کلی مذکور ہو چکا ہے کہ مطلق کی تقیید قیاس کے ساتھ ناجائز ہے تو تنزل تو اس مسئلہ جزیہ مخصوصہ یعنی مسئلہ کفارات کا ذکر کیا اور بتلایا کہ اس مسئلہ میں مانع آخر از قیاس بھی موجود ہے ایکتوور ود نص في المقیس مانع از قیاس تھی اس کے علاوہ ایک اور بھی مانع موجود ہے وھو ان القتل من اعظم الکبائر لہذا اس کے اندر شدت مناسب ہے فیجوزان يشترط پس جائز ہے کہ اس کفارہ قتل میں ایمان کی شرط کی جائے اور جو اس اعظم الکبائر سے کم درجہ کا گناہ ہے اس میں شرط نہ کیا جائے فان تغلیظ الكفارة الم کیونکہ تغلیظ اور تشدید فی الکفارہ غلظ جنایتہ کے مقدار پر ہوتا ہے اور جنت فی الیمین قتل جیسا گناہ نہیں ہے لہذا خفیف جرم کو شدید جرم پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ لا يقال انتم قيد تم الرتبة بالسلامة الخ یہ ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے جو ہم احناف پر محصول میں پیش کیا گیا ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ جب کفارہ یمین میں مطلق رقبہ کا حکم تھا تو تم نے اس کو سلامتہ کے ساتھ کیوں مقید کیا ہے۔ اندھا یا اپاہچ نہ ہو بلکہ صحیح الاعضاء ہو تو تم نے بھی مطلق کی تقلید کر لی تو ہم بھی اگر قید ایمان کر دیں تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے فأجاب بقوله الا ان المطلق یعنی مطلق رقبہ اس کو شامل نہیں ہو سکتا جو رقبہ ہونے کے معنی میں ناقص ہو اور فائت جنس المنفعہ ہو وہ رقبہ ہی نہیں ہے اور فائت جنس المنفعہ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جنس منفعہ پوری فوت ہو مثلا دیکھنا تو دونوں انکھیں مفقود ہوں مثلا پکڑنا تو دونوں ہاتھ ناکارہ ہوں یا مقطوع الیدین ہو اور رجلیں ناکارہ تو چلنے کی منفعت پوری فوت ہے رقبہ ہونے میں ناقص ہے مطلق اس کو شامل نہیں ہو گا لان المطلق بنصرف الى الكامل اسی الکامل فیما بطلق عليه ذا الاسم بذا هو المراد بالقول المشهور المطلق اذا اطلق مراد به الفرد الکامل کالماء المطلق جیسے مار مطلق ماء الورد کو شامل نہیں ہوتا۔
And indeed a difference has been established between the expiations. When this general ruling has been mentioned that restricting the absolute by qiyas is impermissible, then he descended to mention this particular subordinate issue, i.e., the issue of expiations, and stated that in this issue, there is another obstacle to qiyas as well. One obstacle was the existence of a text in the maqis; besides that, there is another obstacle: that murder (qatl) is among the gravest major sins, therefore severity is appropriate in it, so it is permissible to stipulate faith (iman) in its expiation, while that which is a lesser sin (like oath-breaking) should not have this condition. Because the intensification of expiation is proportionate to the gravity of the crime, and the sin in an oath is not like murder; thus it is not correct to analogize a minor offense to a grave one. One should not say: 'You (Hanafis) have restricted the slave with safety (salamah).' This is an answer to an objection presented against us Hanafis in al-Mahsul. The summary is: When in expiation of an oath the ruling was an absolute slave, why did you restrict it with safety? i.e., that the slave must not be blind or incapacitated but be sound in limbs. You have also restricted the absolute, so if we restrict it with faith, there is no harm. He answered: Except that the absolute (mutlaq) does not include that which is deficient in the meaning of being a slave and missing the entire category of benefit; that is not a (proper) slave. Missing the entire category of benefit means that all benefit is lost, e.g., sight is lost in both eyes, or grasping with both hands is lost, or legs are incapacitated so the benefit of walking is completely lost. Such a slave is deficient in being a slave, so the absolute does not include him, because the absolute applies to the perfect (complete) individual concerning which the name applies. This is what is meant by the famous saying: 'When the absolute is used, the perfect individual is intended,' like absolute water does not include rosewater.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage addresses two points. First, it notes that even if the general ruling forbids restricting the absolute by qiyas, in the specific case of expiations there is an additional obstacle: the difference in the severity of sins. Murder is a graver sin than oath-breaking, so it is appropriate to require a believing slave in expiation for murder (as per Quran 4:92), but this condition cannot be extended to oath-breaking by qiyas because the lesser sin does not warrant the same severity. Second, the passage answers an objection: if the Hanafis themselves restrict the absolute slave by requiring the slave to be free from defects (salamah), then why can't the opponent restrict by requiring belief? The answer is that the absolute term 'slave' (raqabah) by its very nature only applies to a complete slave who can perform the intended benefit (e.g., work). A blind or handless slave is not considered a slave in the full sense, so the absolute excludes him. This is not a restriction but an understanding of the definition. Just like absolute water (ma' mutlaq) does not include rosewater. So the condition of safety is inherent, whereas the condition of belief is an additional restriction not supported by the text. This is a classic Hanafi argument to justify the condition of physical integrity without opening the door to arbitrary restrictions by qiyas.

Key Terms
فائت جنس المنفعة (fa'it jins al-manfa'ah): Missing the entire category of benefit, i.e., the slave is so disabled that the primary benefit of slavery (work) is completely lost.
المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل (al-mutlaq yanṣarifu ilā al-kāmil): When the absolute term is used, it refers to the perfect/comprehensive individual that fully fits the definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept the condition of physical soundness (salamah) in the slave for expiation of an oath, but reject the condition of belief (iman)?
A) Because physical soundness is mentioned in the Quranic verse for oath expiation (58:3).
B) Because a blind or maimed slave does not fully qualify as a 'slave' in the absolute sense, whereas a non-Muslim slave does.
C) Because the condition of belief is only for expiation of murder, and the principle of qiyas forbids transferring it to a lesser sin.
D) Because Hanafis follow the opinion of Abu Hanifa, who only required health, while the Sahibayn required belief.

Key Takeaway
When the absolute term is used, it inherently refers to the perfect individual; excluding deficient ones is not taqyeed but tafsir, while adding external conditions like faith requires independent textual evidence.

Ba for Isti'ānah – The Linguistic Principle and Its Contractual Effects
Linguistic principle applied to two sales cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic principle that Ba for isti'ānah indicates a means (wasīlah) to classify terms in a sales contract as price or commodity, and derive the ruling on substitution before possession.

Core Idea
Ba attaches to means, not ends; in sales, the thing after Ba is the price unless it becomes a salam contract.

The seemingly simple letter Ba carries a profound legal function in Hanafi usul. When it appears in a phrase like 'katabtu bi al-qalam' (I wrote with the pen), it signals that the pen is a means for writing. This lesson unpacks how this linguistic insight is extended to sales contracts through qiyas, distinguishing between the price (means) and the sold item (end), and exploring how the position of Ba can even transform a simple sale into a salam contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Linguistic Function of Ba
Recognise that in phrases like 'katabtu bi al-qalam', the letter Ba introduces the means (wasīlah) used to perform the action. This is called Ba for isti'ānah (seeking help).
The same Ba appears in sales phrases. Its function determines whether the following noun is the price or the commodity.
2
Map the Ba Function to Sales Contracts
In sales, the price is the means to acquire the sold item. Therefore, when Ba appears before a noun in a sale statement (e.g., 'bi-karr' in 'ba'tu ... bi-karr'), that noun is normally the price.
This is based on qiyas (analogy) from the linguistic example to the commercial context.
3
Examine Two Contrasting Sale Phrases
Analyse the source text's two examples: (1) 'ba'tu hādhā al-‘abda bi-karr' → wheat is price, simple sale. (2) 'ba'tu al-karra bi al-‘abd' → slave is capital (ra's al-māl), wheat becomes subject matter in salam.
The reversal of the nouns changes the contract type because the object after Ba is now a specific individual, not a fungible (thaman).
4
Derive the Ruling on Substitution (Istibdāl)
When wheat is the price (first example), it can be substituted before possession like any price. When wheat is the subject matter in salam (second example), substitution before possession is prohibited.
This ruling flows from the classification: prices (athmān) are not specific; subject matters in salam are specific and must be delivered exactly as contracted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباء للإنصاف الحاق کا معنی ہے اتصال الشي بالشي والاستعانه ای طلب المعونته بشتی علی شنی یعنی ایک شتی کے ساتھ دوسری شتی پر مدد طلب کرنا جیسے کتبت بالقلم تو قلم معین علی الکتابتہ ہے ۔ فتدخل على الوسائل یہ تفریح على الاستعانتہ ہے ۔ چونکہ وسائل کے ساتھ استعانت علی المقاصد ہوتی ہے اس لئے بارہ استعانتہ وسائل پر داخل ہوتی ہے کا لاشمان جیسے بیوی میں اثمان وسائل ہیں اور مقصود اصلی مبیع ہے تاکہ انتفاع بالمبیع المملوک حاصل ہو سکے اور اشمان جو عموما نقود سے ہوتے ہیں یہ مقصود بالذات نہیں ہوتے بلکہ یہ بمنزلہ آلات کے ہیں جن سے توسل الی المقاصد ہوتا ہے ۔ فان قال بعت هذا العبد بکر تو اس صورت میں عبد مبیع ہوگا اور گر جنط شمن ہوگا جو فی الحال ثابت فی الذمہ ہو جائیگا۔ دنی بعت گرم بالعبد تو اس صورت میں بیع سلم ہو جائیگی اور عبد راس المال ہوگا۔ اور کر حفطہ مسلم فیہ ہوگا۔ خیر اعلی شرائطہ اور اس ثانی صورت میں بیع سلم کے شرائط کی رعایت کی جائیگی مثلا تا جیل شرط ہوگی اور راس المال کا قبض فی المجلس شرط ہوگا ولا یجری الاستبدال فی الکر یعنی کر حنطہ کے بدلہ میں کوئی اور شئی لے لینا یہ قبل قبض الکر جائز نہیں ہوگا بخلاف الدول بخلاف صورۃ اولی کے چونکہ اس اس میں کر ثمن ہے لہذا استبدال في الكر جائز ہوگا جیسے اثمان میں ہوتا ہے۔
The letter Ba is for ilhāq (joining) meaning connection of one thing to another, and isti'ānah (seeking help) meaning seeking assistance from one thing against another, like 'I wrote with the pen'—the pen is an aid for writing. So it enters upon means. This is derived from isti'ānah. Since assistance is sought through means for ends, Ba for isti'ānah enters upon means, like in sales: prices are means, and the main object is the sold item so that benefit from the owned sold item is obtained. Prices, which are usually currency, are not intended for themselves but are like tools through which ends are attained. So if he says 'I sold this slave for wheat,' then the slave is the sold item and the wheat is the price, becoming a debt in the liability. If he says 'I sold the wheat for the slave,' then it becomes a salam sale, the slave is the capital, and the wheat is the salam commodity subject to its conditions, e.g., deferment is required and possession of capital at the session is required. And substitution of the wheat before possession is not allowed, unlike the first case where the wheat is the price, so substitution is allowed as with prices.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage discusses the letter Ba (ب) and its usage for isti'ānah (seeking help). The author, commenting on a usul text, explains that Ba in this sense enters upon the means (wasā'il) that assist in achieving ends. Examples from sales: In 'bā'tu hādhā al-‘abda bi-karr' (I sold this slave for wheat), wheat is the price because it is a means to acquire the slave. In 'bā'tu al-karra bi al-‘abd' (I sold the wheat for the slave), it becomes a salam contract because the price is fungible and the object (slave) is a specific commodity—thus the ruling differs: in salam, possession of capital (slave) at the session is required, and substitution of the wheat (the subject matter) before possession is not allowed, unlike the first case where wheat is price and substitution is allowed. This is a Hanafi ruling based on the principle that Ba attaches to means.

Key Terms
الباء للاستعانة (al-bā' li al-isti'ānah): The letter Ba used to indicate seeking help through a means (wasīlah).
وسائل (wasā'il): Means by which an end is achieved; in sales, price is a means to acquire the object.
ثمن (thaman): Price, the monetary or fungible compensation given in a sale.
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example 'ba'tu hādhā al-‘abda bi-karr', why is substitution (istibdāl) of the wheat permissible before possession?
A) Because the wheat is the sold item (muthman).
B) Because the wheat is the price (thaman).
C) Because the contract is salam.
D) Because the slave is the price.

Key Takeaway
The Ba for isti'ānah attaches to means; in sales, the noun after Ba is normally the price, but if that noun is a specific individual, the contract is salam and the ruling on substitution reverses.

The Invalidity of Qiyas When a Legal Difference (Farq) Exists: Feeding vs Clothing in Kaffarah
Rebuttal of qiyas showing difference between feeding and clothing in expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a flawed qiyas by detecting a clear legal difference (farq) between the original and new case, using the Hanafi rebuttal of analogizing feeding to clothing in expiation.

Core Idea
Feeding achieves its purpose permanently; clothing does not—this difference invalidates the analogy.

In this passage, the commentator refutes an opponent's analogy between feeding and clothing in expiation. The opponent argued that since both involve giving something for benefit, the ruling on clothing should extend to feeding. The Hanafi scholar offers two responses: one based on the linguistic nature of the words (masdar vs concrete noun), and another based on the permanence of benefit. This lesson teaches you to spot when a qiyas fails because the effective cause ('illah) is not fully present in the original case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's qiyas
The opponent analogizes feeding (it'am) to clothing (kiswah) in kaffarah, claiming both involve permissive use. State the asl, far', and claimed 'illah.
The opponent likely follows a general principle of permissibility.
2
Examine the first Hanafi response
The first response distinguishes based on word type: it'am is a masdar (verbal noun) inherently implying permissibility without ownership, while kiswah is a concrete noun requiring ownership transfer. Analyze why this linguistic difference matters legally.
3
Examine the second Hanafi response
Even if both are masdars, the purpose of feeding is fully achieved by permissive use (eating) because consumption is irreversible. Clothing can be reclaimed by the lender, defeating the purpose. Identify the farq (legal difference) in permanence of benefit.
4
Conclude the invalidity of qiyas
Because there is a clear farq between the two cases, the qiyas is invalid ('qiyas ma' al-fariq'). The Hanafi ruling for it'am remains based on permissibility without ownership transfer.
This illustrates a key usul principle: qiyas fails if the 'illah is not fully present in both cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كے لئے کافی نہیں ہے۔ على ان الاباحة في الطعام تتم المقصود به قياس مندر کو ر کا دوسرا جواب ہے پہلے جواب میں یہ یہ فرق پیش نظر تھا کہ اطعام مصدر ہے جس کے معنی میں خود اباحہ تھی لہذا تملیک ضروری نہیں تھی بخلاف کسوۃ کے یہ مصدر نہیں ہے بلکہ اسم ثوب ہے لہذا اس میں تملیک ضرور ہی ہے کہ کفارہ میں خود ثوب دیدیا جائے اور بصورت اعادہ اباحہ صرف منافع آتے ہیں نفس ثوب ملک میں نہیں آتا حالانکہ ضروری یہی ہے اور دوسرے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ کسوہ مصدر ہے جیسے اطعام مصدر تھا لیکن پھر بھی ان دونوں میں فرق ہے وہ یہ کہ اباحۃ فی الطعام میں مقصود تام ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ مقصود تو پیٹ بھرنا ہے اور طعام اگرچہ ملک مسکین میں رہے اور مساکین پیٹ بھر کر اس کے مملوکہ طعام کو کھالیں تو مقصود حاصل ہو جاتا ہے. دون اعادة الثوب اعارة ثوب میں مقصود تام حاصل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اعارة واباحتہ میں یہ ہوگا کہ مساکین کپڑا پہنے رہیں لیکن ثوب میں ملک مسکین میں رہے تو اس صورت میں مسکین جو معیر ہے جس وقت چاہے اسے کپڑا واپس کرنے کا اختیار ہے جب کپڑا طالب کرلے تو مقصود فوت ہو گیا بخلاف طعام کے کہ جو کھایا جا چکا ہے اس کی واپسی ناممکن ہے تو جب کسوہ واطعام میں فرق ہو گیا تو اطعام کو کسوہ پر قیاس کرنا مع الفارق ہے ۔
is not sufficient. Upon the permissibility in food, the purpose is fully achieved by it – this is the second answer to the qiyas of the Mālikī school. In the first answer, this difference was considered: feeding (it'am) is a verbal noun (masdar) whose meaning inherently includes permissibility, so ownership is not necessary, unlike clothing (kiswah) which is not a masdar but a noun for a garment, so ownership is necessary – the garment itself must be given in expiation. In the case of lending, permissibility only pertains to benefits, the garment itself does not come into ownership, which is necessary. The gist of the second answer is: we concede that kiswah is a masdar just as it'am was a masdar, but still there is a difference between them: in permissibility of food, the purpose is fully achieved because the aim is to fill the belly; even if the food remains in the ownership of the owner, and the poor eat the food owned by him, the purpose is achieved. As for the return of clothing, in lending a garment the purpose is not fully achieved because in lending and permissibility, the poor would wear the garment but it remains in the owner's possession; in that case, the owner (mu'ir) can take back the garment whenever he wishes. When he demands the garment back, the purpose is lost, unlike food which has already been consumed and its return is impossible. So when there is a difference between kiswah and it'am, analogizing it'am to kiswah is an analogy with a difference (al-fariq).
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of an opposing school's argument that analogizes feeding (it'am) to clothing (kiswah) in expiation (kaffarah). The commentator gives two answers. First: it'am is a masdar inherently implying permissibility without ownership, while kiswah is a concrete noun requiring ownership transfer. Second: even if both are masdars, the purpose of feeding is fully achieved by mere permissive use (eating) since the food is consumed and cannot be returned, whereas clothing lent remains under the lender's control and can be reclaimed, defeating the purpose. Thus the qiyas fails due to a significant legal difference (farq). This illustrates a key Hanafi usul principle: qiyas is invalid when the underlying cause ('illah) does not fully apply.

Key Terms
اطعام (it'am): Feeding (as an act of expiation); a masdar implying permissibility to eat
کسوہ (kiswah): Clothing (as an act of expiation); a noun for a garment requiring ownership transfer
مصدر (masdar): Verbal noun; in usul, a masdar can indicate permissibility without requiring ownership transfer
مع الفارق (ma' al-fariq): An analogy with a difference; such qiyas is invalid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, why is it'am (feeding) different from kiswah (clothing) in kaffarah, making qiyas between them invalid?
A) It'am is a masdar while kiswah is a concrete noun
B) The purpose of feeding is fully achieved through permissive use, but clothing can be reclaimed by the lender
C) Kiswah requires ownership transfer while it'am does not
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a qiyas is invalid if there is a clear legal difference (farq) between the original and new case; feeding and clothing in kaffarah exemplify this due to the irreversibility of consumption versus the revocable nature of clothing.

Qisas with a Heavy Object: The Usul Dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Debate on whether murder with a heavy object requires qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of dalalat al-nass to distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the 'illah of qisas.

Core Idea
For Imam Abu Hanifa, qisas requires an instrument that breaks the body both outwardly and inwardly; a heavy object breaks only inwardly.

This lesson examines an intra-madhhab dispute over the 'illah (effective cause) of qisas. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) used dalalat al-nass (implied meaning) to extend the ruling from swords to heavy objects. Imam Abu Hanifa insisted on a more precise 'illah: a wound that breaks the human structure both outwardly (visible tear) and inwardly (death). Understanding this debate clarifies how Hanafi usul defines the effective cause in penal law and how differing interpretations of the same text lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
State whether qisas is wajib for murder with a heavy object according to the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa. Write down their positions clearly.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil
Explain how the Sahibayn use dalalat al-nass from the hadith 'La tuqadu illa bis-sayf' to derive the 'illah: striking with something the body cannot bear. Note that they interpret the hadith as a general meaning rather than a specific prohibition.
Dalalat al-nass is a direct understanding from the text, not analogical reasoning.
3
Analyze Imam's 'illah
State Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of the complete 'illah: a wound that breaks the body both outwardly (zahiran) and inwardly (batinan). Contrast this with the Sahibayn's broader 'illah.
Imam's 'illah excludes heavy objects because they only break inwardly.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Describe the practical consequence: under Imam Abu Hanifa, murder with a heavy object does not trigger qisas but leads to diya and possibly ta'zir; under the Sahibayn, qisas is applied.
The Hanafi madhhab relies on Imam's view for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكوجوب القصاص بالمثقل عندهما صاحبین " کے نزدیک مثقل چیز کے ساتھ کسی کو قتل کیا جائے تو قاتل پر قصاص واجب ہو جائے گا۔ لاعند الامام " صاحبین اس کو دلالۃ النص سے ثابت کرتے ہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ قول رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم لا تود الا بالسیف دو معانی کا محتمل ہے ایک یہ کہ قصاص قائم نہیں کیا جائیگا مگر صرف تلوار کے ساتھ یعنی قاتل سے قصاص میں تلوار کی ضرب سے اس کی گردن کائی جائے گی والثاني لاقدر الا بسبب القتل بالسین یعنی قصاص اس وقت قائم کیا جائیگا جب قاتل الدیہ نے مقتول کو تلوار کے ساتھ قتل کیا ہو ۔ صاحبین اسی ثانی معنی کے لحاظ سے استدلال بدلالۃ النص کرتے ہیں حاصل استدلال یہ ہے کہ خان المعنى الذى منصوص ہیں جو معنی علت حکم ہے اس کو جاری کرنے کی کوشش ہے تاکہ یہ دلالتہ النص میں درج ہو جائے یعنی وہ معنی جو سمجھا جاتا ہے کہ وہ موجب ہے جزا کامل کا اس بارہ میں کہ جب حرمہ نفس تباہ کی جائے تو وہ معنی ضرب ہے ایسی شئی کے ساتھ کہ جسم و بدن اس کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو۔ يفهم موجبا لفظ موجبا ترکیب میں ضمیر نیفہیم سے حال ہے مفہوم یہ ہوگا کہ وہ معنی جو سمجھا جاتا ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ موجب ہے للجزاء جزاء كامل كا عن انتهاك حرمة النفس يه جار مجرور لفظ الجزاء کے ساتھ متعلق ہے یعنی حرمتہ نفس کی انتہاک پر جزاء کا موجب جو معنی سمجھ آتا ہے اور الانتهاك افتعال کا باب ہے ان تھک لفظ نون اس کا فاکلمہ ہے دھو القطع اس کا معنی ہے قطع کرنا اور کاٹ دینا بولتے ہیں سیف نھیک ای قاطع انتھاک کا معنی فارسی میں حرمت کسی شکستن یعنی کسی نفس کی حرمہ کو توڑنا اور کاٹنا ایسے طریق پر کہ وہ حلال نہیں۔ الضرب یہ خبر ہے ان کی جو مذکو رہے فی قولہ فان المعنی یعنی وہ معنی جو موجب ہے جزاء کا وہ ہے الضرب بما لا یطیقہ البدن اور یہ معنی جیسے ضرب بالسیف میں موجود ہے اسی طرح ضرب بالمثقل میں بھی موجود ہے تو دلالہ یہ ضرب بالمثقل موجب قصاص ہوگی ۔
وقال البوحنیفہ المعنی امام فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ معنی جو منصوص میں موجب قصاص ہے وہ ہے جرم ينقض البنية ظاهر و باطنا یعنی ایسار خم جو نبیہ انسانی کی ظاہر و باطنا نقض کرے اور توڑ دے ظاہرا یوں کہ جسم میں زخم ہو جاتے اور جستہ کی تخریب ہو اور باطنا یوں کہ از باق اور اخراج نفس حیوانیہ کا ہو جاتے جس کے ساتھ حس و حرکۃ وابستہ ہے نانه حينئدة تقع الجناية قصداً على النفس الحيوانية قصدا کے ساتھ قتل خطا کا اخراج کیا کہ وہ قصداً نہیں اور نقض بنیہ ظاہر و باطنا کے ساتھ اس جرح سے احتراز کیا جو سرایتہ نہ کرے اور موت تک نہ پہونچاتے کیونکہ یہ نقص بنیہ صرف فاصل کرتا ہے باطنا نہیں کرتا اور ضرب بالمثقل سے بھی احتراز کیا کیونکہ وہ نقض بنسیہ صرف باطنا کرتا ہے کہ از ہاق روح تو ہو جاتا ہے لیکن ظاہر وہ نقض نہیں کرتا۔ لہذا جرح جو نقص بنیہ ظاہر او باطنا کرے اور ہو بالعمد یہ اکمل الجنایتہ ہے لہذا جزاء اکمل یعنی قصاص اسی کے ساتھ مختص ہونا چاہیے۔
And the obligation of qisas with a heavy object according to them (Sahibayn): If someone is killed with a heavy object, qisas is wajib upon the killer. Not according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. The Sahibayn prove this by dalalat al-nass. They say: The saying of the Messenger of Allah (s) 'La tuqadu illa bis-sayf' (qisas is not executed except with the sword) is probable of two meanings: one that qisas is not carried out except with a sword, i.e., the killer's neck is struck with a sword; the second that qisas is not established except due to killing with a sword, i.e., qisas is established only when the killer killed the victim with a sword. The Sahibayn adopt the second meaning and deduce by dalalat al-nass. The summary of the deduction: the meaning that is understood from the text (the 'illah of the ruling) is an attempt to apply it so that it falls under dalalat al-nass. That meaning which is understood as being the cause of complete recompense regarding violation of the sanctity of the soul is striking with something that the body cannot bear. So the word 'muwjib' is a hal from the understood pronoun, meaning: the meaning that is understood, while it is the cause of the punishment of complete recompense for violation of the sanctity of the soul. And 'al-intihāk' is from the verb 'intahaka' meaning to tear and cut. So 'al-intihāk' means breaking the sanctity in a forbidden manner. Then 'al-darb' is the predicate of 'inna' in 'fa inna al-ma'nā', meaning: the meaning that is the cause of punishment is striking with that which the body cannot bear. And this meaning is present in striking with a sword, similarly it is present in striking with a heavy object. So by this dalalat, striking with a heavy object necessitates qisas. And Imam Abu Hanifa says: The meaning that is the cause of qisas in the text is a wound that breaks the structure (body) outwardly and inwardly, i.e., the structure of the human body is broken both outwardly (wounds, tearing of skin) and inwardly (removal of the animal soul with which sensation and movement are connected). Thus the injury is intentionally against the animal soul (excluding accidental killing). And by 'breaking the structure outwardly and inwardly', he excludes wounds that do not spread and do not lead to death, because such breaking is only internal? Actually he excludes heavy object striking because it only breaks inwardly (removes the soul) but does not break outwardly. Thus the injury that breaks the structure both outwardly and inwardly and is intentional is the most complete form of crime, so the most complete recompense (qisas) should be specific to it.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the usul dispute regarding qisas (retaliatory execution) when the murder weapon is a heavy object (muthaqqal), such as a club or stone. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that qisas is wajib in such cases, relying on dalalat al-nass (implied meaning) of the hadith 'La tuqadu illa bis-sayf' (Qisas is not carried out except with a sword). They interpret the hadith not as limiting the execution method to a sword, but as establishing that qisas is due only for killing with a sword-like instrument that causes immediate death by overwhelming the body's capacity. Since a heavy object also strikes the body in a way that the body cannot bear, the same ruling applies by dalalat al-nass (the understood meaning from the text). Imam Abu Hanifa, however, restricts qisas to cases where the instrument breaks the body both outwardly (causing visible wounds) and inwardly (causing death). A heavy object may break the body internally (by crushing or causing internal injury) but does not necessarily cause external wounds; therefore it does not satisfy the complete 'illah (effective cause) of qisas. Thus, according to Imam, murder with a heavy object does not require qisas, but rather diya (blood money) or ta'zir. This difference shows how the Sahibayn applied the principle of dalalat al-nass more broadly, while Imam required a stricter correspondence between the 'illah and the act.

Key Terms
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): The implied meaning of a text beyond its literal wording, understood by context or common sense; here, the Sahibayn derive an 'illah from the hadith that extends to similar cases.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, specifically execution for intentional murder; its 'illah is a complete crime breaking the body both outwardly and inwardly according to Imam.
مثقل (muthaqqal): A heavy object used as a weapon, such as a club or stone, that kills by crushing or internal injury without necessarily cutting the skin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why does murder with a heavy object not require qisas?
A) Because the hadith limits qisas to swords only.
B) Because the heavy object does not break the body both outwardly and inwardly.
C) Because heavy objects are not considered deadly weapons.
D) Because the Sahibayn's opinion is weak.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies qisas only when the murder instrument breaks the body both outwardly and inwardly, a condition that heavy objects fail to meet, as per Imam Abu Hanifa's stricter 'illah.

Condition vs. Time: How Shart Affects Cause in Contracts
Explaining the difference between condition and time in contracts, and their effect on the cause and ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the effect of conditions (shart) on the cause (sabab) in contracts of establishment (sale) and contracts of removal (divorce/manumission), and explain the Hanafi rationale based on admission of risk (khatar).

Core Idea
In sale, conditions affect only the ruling (hukm); in divorce/manumission, conditions affect the cause (sabab) itself.

This lesson explores a foundational usul al-fiqh distinction: the difference between condition (shart) and time (ajal) in contracts, and how each interacts with the cause (sabab) and the ruling (hukm). The Hanafi school argues that conditions in sale cannot enter upon the cause because sale does not admit risk (khatar), whereas divorce and manumission, being acts of removal (isqat), admit risk and thus allow conditions to affect the cause. This leads to an important inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who analogized conditions in all contracts to deferment and option conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i position
State that Imam al-Shafi'i analogized suspension by condition (ta'liq bi al-shart) to deferment of price (ta'jil) and the option condition (khiyar al-shart) in sale. He argued that these delay the ruling but do not prevent the cause, so the same should apply to all conditions.
The Shafi'i qiyas treats condition as analogous to time.
2
Understand the Hanafi distinction
The Hanafi author distinguishes: time (ajal) and option condition (khiyar al-shart) enter only upon the ruling (hukm), not upon the cause (sabab). For example, deferment of price delays payment but the sale is concluded instantly.
This is the key principle: some elements affect only the ruling.
3
Explain the role of risk (khatar)
Sale is a contract of exchange (muawada) that does not admit uncertainty (khatar). If a condition could affect the cause, the sale would become dependent on a future event, resembling gambling (qimar). Therefore, conditions in sale can only enter on the ruling, not the cause.
Khatar is the pivotal illa (effective cause) for the distinction.
4
Contrast with divorce/manumission
Divorce and manumission are acts of removal (isqat), not establishment (ithbat). Removal admits risk and uncertainty, so conditions can enter upon the cause itself. Hence, a suspended divorce does not occur until the condition is fulfilled.
The nature of the act (isqat vs. ithbat) determines the rule.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a sale suspended on a condition (e.g., 'if my father arrives'), the sale is valid immediately; in a divorce suspended on a condition (e.g., 'if you enter the house'), the divorce does not occur until the condition is met.
This difference affects the legal status of parties in the interim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رتبتين الفرق على من حبنا بين الشرط وبين الاجل امام شافعی نے تعلیق بالشرط کو بمنزلہ تأجيل في الشمس اور شرط الخیار فی البیع کے قرار دیا کہ جیسے تاجیل اور شرط خیار انعقاد سبب کو نہیں روکتے بلکہ سبب ملک یعنی بیع منعقد ہو جاتی ہے البتہ حکم مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح تعلیق بالشرط میں بھی شرط انعقاد سبية کو نہیں روکتی بلکہ تاخیر حکم الى وجود الشرط ہو جاتی ہے تو مصنف نے فرق کرتے ہوئے کہا خان مدين اى الاجل وشرط الخيار د اخلان علی الحکم یعنی حکم پر داخل ہیں اور سبب پر داخل ہی نہیں ہیں۔ اما الاجل فظاهر کیونکہ تاجیل تو شمن پر داخل ہے بیع پر تو داخل نہیں ہے انعقاد بیع تو قطعا ہو چکا ہے البتہ مطالبہ ثمن میعاد مقررہ تک موخر ہو جائیگا را ما خيار الشرط فلان البيع الخبيع جو کہ ملک ہے۔ خیار شرط اس پر داخل نہیں کیونکہ بیع لا يحتمل الخطر یعنی بیع شرط کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی کیونکہ شرط کے ساتھ معلق کرنے میں بیع متردر ہو جائیگی بین ان نقع وان لا يقع اسی کا نام خطر ہے یعنی تردد اور شک کے ساتھ وابستہ ہونا اس صورت میں بیع بمنزلہ قمار ہو جائیگی جو متر در بین النفع والخسران ہوتا ہے ۔ فشرط الخیار پس شرط الخیار کی مشروعیة مع المنافی ہے کیونکہ بیع احتمال خطر و شرط نہیں رکھتی لہذا اس خیار کی مشروعیتہ علی خلاف القیاس ہے صرف رفع غبن کی ضرورت کے پیش نظر ہے اور ضرورت اس کے ساتھ مندفع ہو جاتی ہے کہ یہ داخل علی الحکم ہو لا علی السبب کیونکہ اگر داخل على السبب مانا جائے تو پھر داخل على السبب والحکم معا ہو جائے گا ۔ ند خوله علی المحکم استیل اس کا ذخول صرف علی الحکم مانا جائے تو یہ اسکمل ہے بنسبت اس کے کہ داخل علی السبب والحکم کلی جا مانا جائے ناما الطلاق والعتاق طلاق اور عتاق یہ محتمل شرط ہیں کیوں کہ یہ از قبیلہ اسقاط میں از قبیلہ اثبات نہیں ہیں اور اسقاط احتمال خطر و شرط رکھتا ہے لہذا طلاق وعتاق میں شرط داخل علی السبب ہوگی تاکہ تخلف حكم عن السبب لازم نہ آئے لہذا تعلیق بالشرط انعقاد سبب سے مانع ہے تو سبب پر داخل ہونے سے یہاں کوئی مانع نہیں ہے بخلاف بیع کے کہ شرط یہاں داخل علی السبب نہیں ہے ورنہ تو بمنزلہ قمار کے ہو جائیگی اور یہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔
He arranged the distinction between condition and time: Imam al-Shafi'i considered suspension by condition as analogous to deferment in price and the condition of option in sale, that just as deferment and option condition do not prevent the conclusion of the cause, rather the cause of ownership, i.e., the sale is concluded, but the ruling is delayed. Similarly, in suspension by condition, the condition does not prevent the conclusion of the cause, but rather the ruling is delayed until the existence of the condition. So the author, distinguishing, said: 'Time and the condition of option enter upon the ruling, i.e., they enter on the ruling and do not enter on the cause. As for time, it is obvious, because deferment enters on the price, not on the sale; the conclusion of the sale has definitely occurred, but the demand for the price is delayed until the appointed term. And as for the option condition, because the sale, which is ownership, does not admit risk (khatar), i.e., the sale cannot tolerate the condition, because when suspended by condition, the sale becomes uncertain between occurrence and non-occurrence, and that is called risk, i.e., being associated with doubt and uncertainty. In that case, the sale becomes like gambling, which is wavering between profit and loss. So the condition of option, its legality is despite the contradiction, because the sale does not admit the possibility of risk and condition. Therefore, its legality is against analogy (khilaf al-qiyas), only for the necessity of removing harm, and necessity is fulfilled by it being that it enters on the ruling, not on the cause, because if it were considered entering on the cause, then it would enter on both cause and ruling together. But its entry only on the ruling is more complete than considering it entering on both cause and ruling. As for divorce and manumission, these admit the condition, because they are of the category of removal (isqat), not of the category of establishment (ithbat), and removal admits the possibility of risk and condition. Therefore, in divorce and manumission, the condition enters on the cause, so that non-occurrence of the ruling from the cause is not necessary. Therefore, suspension by condition prevents the conclusion of the cause, so there is no impediment here for it to enter on the cause, unlike sale, where the condition does not enter on the cause, otherwise it would become like gambling, and that is not correct.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and dispute (ikhtilaf) between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of conditions (shart) and time (ajal) on contracts. Imam al-Shafi'i analogized suspension by condition (ta'liq bi al-shart) to deferment of price (ta'jil) and the option condition (khiyar al-shart) in sale, arguing that just as these do not prevent the formation of the contract but only delay the ruling, so too does suspension by condition not prevent the cause from being concluded. The Hanafi author (possibly the commentator) distinguishes: time (ajal) and the option condition (khiyar al-shart) enter upon the ruling (hukm), not upon the cause (sabab). For example, deferment of price does not affect the validity of sale; it only delays the obligation to pay. Similarly, the option condition is legally recognized against analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) to remove harm, and it only enters on the ruling, not on the cause. However, in divorce (talaq) and manumission ('itaq), which are acts of removal (isqat), conditions can enter on the cause itself because removal admits risk (khatar). Therefore, in divorce and manumission, suspension by condition prevents the cause from being established until the condition is fulfilled, whereas in sale, the condition does not affect the cause. This distinction ensures that sale does not become like gambling.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition attached to a contract or action; if it is of removal (isqat), it can affect the cause.
أجل (ajal): A fixed time or term, which delays the ruling but does not affect the cause.
خطر (khatar): Risk or uncertainty; contracts that admit khatar can have conditions affecting the cause.
اسقاط (isqat): Removal or termination of a right; acts like divorce and manumission are isqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does suspension by condition affect the cause in divorce but not in sale?
A) Sale is more important than divorce.
B) Divorce and manumission are acts of removal (isqat) that admit risk (khatar), while sale does not.
C) The Shafi'i school says otherwise.
D) Conditions can never affect the cause in any contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the distinction between contracts of establishment (ithbat) and removal (isqat) determines whether a condition can affect the cause (sabab) or only the ruling (hukm).

The Interplay of Vow and Honor of Time: Qada of Missed Vowed I'tikaf
Explanation of qada ruling with usul reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a temporary exemption due to the honor of time ceases when the exempting time ends, and the original requirement revives for qada.

Core Idea
The honor of time drops the specific fast but qada revives it; delay risks missing both.

This passage addresses a subtle scenario: a person vows to observe i'tikaf in Ramadan but misses it. Does the qada require the specific fast, or does the lost honor of Ramadan excuse it? The Hanafi reasoning reveals a deeper usul principle: when a superior time temporarily lifts a requirement, the requirement returns once that time passes. We'll trace how the authors use the hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi al-sawm' and the concept of precaution to resolve the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligations created by the vow
The hadith establishes that i'tikaf requires fasting, so the nadhr for i'tikaf necessitates both the i'tikaf and its specific fast.
This is the default requirement before considering any special time.
2
Examine the effect of sharf al-waqt
In the original Ramadan, the specific fast drops because the Ramadan fast itself is superior. The vower only needs to perform i'tikaf without its specific fast in that month.
This is a temporary exemption by istihsan due to the honor of time.
3
Consider the case when the i'tikaf is missed
After Ramadan passes, the temporary exemption ends. The vow reverts to its original requirement (including the specific fast). But should we wait for another Ramadan or perform qada immediately?
Two options arise: immediate qada with fast, or delayed qada with the next Ramadan's honor.
4
Evaluate the two options using precaution
The passage argues that immediate qada with the specific fast is more precautionary (ahwat) because delaying risks death and the loss of the obligation entirely.
The author, citing Fakhr al-Islam, prefers the first option.
5
Extract the usul rule
The temporary dropping of a condition due to sharf al-waqt does not permanently alter the obligation; the original requirement revives when the special time ends. This is a form of istihsan based on the hadith and the need to preserve the vow's intent.
This rule applies broadly in Hanafi usul for vows and other acts affected by temporal virtues.

الوقت اور وجہ آخر یہ ہے کہ قضام واجب ہو اور اس کے ساتھ شرف وقت کی رعایت بھی واجب کردی جائے یعنی رمضان آخر کی انتظار کی جائے والدليل على الاحوطیۃ اور احوط ہونے کی دلیل وہ ہے جو فخرال اسلام نے کہا لان ما ثبت بشرف الوقت الى آخره معناہ اور اس کے قول کا معنی یہ ہے ان شرف الموقت کے شرف وقت نے ایک زیادہ واجب و ثابت کی تھی اور ایک نقصان ثابت کیا تھا فالزيادة زیادہ یہ ہے کر صوم رمضان کو افضلیت حاصل ہے علی صیام سائر الایام باقی ایام کے معیام پر صیام رمضان افضل ہے والنقصان اور شرف وقت نے جو نقصان ثابت کیا تھا ۔ موعدم وجوب الصوم المقصودوه صوم مقصوده في الاعتکاف کا معدوم ہو جانا اور ساقط ہو جانا فلما معنی رمضان یعنی جب رمضا
Then if he performed but did not perform i'tikaf, then in the next Ramadan qada of i'tikaf should be permissible, because qada became obligatory with that which made the performance obligatory. And the performance of i'tikaf was made obligatory by the vow, and the vow of i'tikaf in Ramadan does not necessitate the fast that is specific to i'tikaf. So qada of i'tikaf should be permissible in another Ramadan. We said: Here qada is obligatory by that which made performance obligatory. This is the answer to the mentioned question. The summary is that qada in this place is obligatory with the same vow with which performance was obligatory. And the vow of i'tikaf necessitates the specific fast of i'tikaf. However, this specific fast of i'tikaf fell away in the first Ramadan in which he made the vow, because of the honor of the time, since in the famous Ramadan, the Ramadan fast is the most excellent worship, therefore the specific fast of i'tikaf dropped. When this temporary honor of time is lost—and its attainment is not possible except after a long period, from Shawwal to the next Ramadan, during which life and death are equally possible—then the vow returns to its original state and necessitates the specific fast of i'tikaf. Because i'tikaf itself necessitates the intended fast, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' When a person makes a vow of i'tikaf, the intended fast specific to i'tikaf becomes obligatory with it. Yes, if the i'tikaf is in Ramadan, e.g., he says 'For Allah upon me that I will perform i'tikaf in this Ramadan of this year,' then since the fast of Ramadan has superiority over the fasts of other days, therefore the specific fast of i'tikaf drops. The dropping of the specific intended fast of i'tikaf, although a type of loss, is compensated by the honor of time, i.e., the honor of Ramadan, which is greater virtue. And the loss and harm caused by abandoning the intended specific fast of i'tikaf due to the virtue of Ramadan is removed. So the obligation of qada with the dropping of the honor of time is more precautionary than its obligation with the honor of time. That is, when a vowed i'tikaf could not be performed in Ramadan, qada is obligatory upon him. But qada has two forms: one is that when the specific Ramadan without i'tikaf has passed, the virtue of honor of time is lost, then one should not wait for the honor of time next year, but rather qada should be made obligatory with the specific fast of i'tikaf. The second form of qada is that one waits for the next Ramadan; when the next Ramadan comes, then greater virtue will be obtained in its days. Now in this Ramadan, perform qada i'tikaf, and the intended fast will drop, and the virtue and honor of time will compensate for this loss. But the period until the next Ramadan is long, the fear of death is present at all times, perhaps the next Ramadan may not be reached. Therefore the first form is more precautionary. The author presented this, saying: 'So the obligation of qada with the dropping of the honor of time' i.e., when Ramadan has passed and the honor of time is lost, despite that, making qada obligatory with the intended fast is more precautionary. This is the first form, 'than its obligation with the honor of time' i.e., in comparison to making qada obligatory with the honor of time—i.e., waiting for the next Ramadan and having the obligation of qada in it—this qada would be with honor of time. This is the second form. The first form is more precautionary than it. Because the dropping of the honor of time will cause the intended fast, and the virtue of the intended fast is more precautionary than the virtue of the honor of time, relative to waiting for the next Ramadan and obtaining the virtue of honor of time. This is the meaning of Fakhr al-Islam's saying: 'And this was the precaution of the two aspects,' and the reference means that in Fakhr al-Islam's statement, the word 'this' refers to the dropping that is understood from his saying: 'Only what is established by the honor of time of the increase to the increase of virtue.' So the conclusion of Fakhr al-Islam's speech is that the obligation of qada with the dropping of the increase, i.e., cancelling the increase that is established by the honor of time, this qada is more precautionary than the other aspect, i.e., the other reason is that qada is obligatory and with it the observance of the honor of time is also made obligatory, i.e., waiting for the next Ramadan. And the evidence for the precaution is what Fakhr al-Islam said: 'Because what is established by the honor of time...' and the meaning of his statement is that the honor of time established an increase and established a loss. The increase is that the fast of Ramadan has superiority over the fasts of other days. The loss is the non-existence of the obligation of the intended fast, i.e., the intended fast in i'tikaf becomes non-existent and drops. So when the meaning of Ramadan?
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal reasoning (talil) on the issue of qada (makeup) for a missed i'tikaf that was vowed (nadhr) for a specific Ramadan. The discussion centers on whether the qada must include the specific fast (sawm) that is normally part of i'tikaf, or whether the honor of the time (sharf al-waqt) of Ramadan can compensate for dropping that fast. The text presents two possibilities: (1) perform qada immediately after the missed Ramadan with the specific fast, losing the honor of the original time but ensuring the intended fast; (2) wait until the next Ramadan to perform qada, thereby regaining the honor of time but allowing the specific fast to drop. The author, citing Fakhr al-Islam, declares the first option more precautionary (ahwat) because fear of death makes delay risky. The Prophet's hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi al-sawm' (There is no i'tikaf except with fasting) is used as proof that the specific fast is integral to the vow. The reasoning applies Hanafi usul principles: when the honor of time (sharf al-waqt) causes the specific fast to drop, it is a loss that is compensated by the virtue of Ramadan, but after Ramadan passes, the vow reverts to its original requirement of the specific fast for qada.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): The legal makeup or compensatory performance of a missed obligatory act of worship.
نذر (nadhr): A vow by which a person obligates upon themselves an act of worship that was not originally obligatory.
شرف الوقت (sharf al-waqt): The honor and virtue associated with a specific time (e.g., Ramadan) that can elevate the reward of worship or alter the requirements of a vow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is performing qada of a vowed i'tikaf immediately with the specific fast more precautionary than waiting for the next Ramadan?
A) Because the next Ramadan will definitely come, but the fast would be less virtuous.
B) Because there is a risk of death before the next Ramadan, so delaying might cause the obligation to be missed entirely.
C) Because the specific fast cannot be performed outside Ramadan.
D) Because the vow becomes invalid if not performed in the original Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The honor of time temporarily suspends a requirement, but after the time passes, the original obligation revives; hence, qada of a missed vowed i'tikaf must include the specific fast unless performed in another Ramadan.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Fidyah for Prayer: Qiyas or Ihtiyat?
Dispute on extending fidyah from fasting to prayer via analogy vs. precaution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qiyas and ihtiyat in Hanafi usul and explain why fidyah for prayer is valid on precautionary grounds.

Core Idea
Hanafi school extends fidyah from fasting to prayer not by strict qiyas but by precaution based on probable cause of inability.

This passage presents a common objection: if a ruling is not textually established for prayer, how can fidyah be required? The Hanafi response unveils a key usul principle: when certainty is lacking, precaution (ihtiyat) can justify a ruling, especially in worship. You will learn to differentiate between qiyas and ihtiyat as methods of istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Objection
The opponent argues that rulings without textual equivalent cannot be extended by qiyas. Since fidyah for prayer has no text and no rational equivalent, analogizing from fasting is invalid.
This objection is based on the principle that acts of worship without rational meaning are not open to qiyas.
2
Locate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response claims that the ruling on fidyah for fasting is probably caused by inability (ta'lil bil-ajz). Since inability also exists for prayer, the same ruling applies.
The key is that the 'illa is probabilistic (zanni), not certain.
3
Note the Use of Ihtiyat
Imam Muhammad uses the phrase 'narju al-qabul' (we hope for acceptance), which is only used in precautionary matters, not strict qiyasi ones. This shows the ruling is based on ihtiyat.
Ihtiyat is a valid method in Hanafi usul when certainty is absent, especially in worship.
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow fidyah for prayer; other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not permit it at all.
This difference stems from methodological divergence on the use of ihtiyat vs. strict qiyas.

Source Text

ہو جائے تو اس کی قضا فدیہ کے ساتھ صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ فدیہ مثل معقول للصلوۃ نہیں اور نص بھی صلوۃ میں وارد نہیں ہے بلکہ نص فدیہ صرف صوم میں وارد ہے تو یہ ایسا حکم ہوا جو غير مدرك بالقياس ہے فینبغی ان نہیں ہے تو تم نے تصدق بالعین او بقیمتہ کا وجوب کیوں کیا ہے تور التصدق بالعین کا عطف الفدیہ پر ہے جو لم اوجبتهم الغدیر میں مذکور ہے قلنا یہ جواب ہے خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ صوم کے بارہ میں جو فدیہ کا حکم ہے محتمل التعليل بالعجز احتمال رکھتا ہے کہ معلل بالعجز ہو یعنی شیخ فانی جو عاجز عن الصیام ہے اس معجزہ کی بنا پر فدیہ بجائے صیام کے لازم کیا گیا ہے تو میسی عجز عن الصلوۃ بھی ہے فقلنا بالوجوب احتیاطا تو اسی عجز کی بنا پر صلوۃ میں بھی ہم نے قول بوجوب الفدیہ کا کر دیا ہے اور یہ معنی بر احتیاط ہے نیکون آیا بالمندوب اوالو تو فدیہ ادا کرنے میں ادائیگی واجب ہو جائیگی اگر واجب نہ بھی ہو تو مندوب ہو جائیگا پھر بھی احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ فدیہ عن الصلوۃ ہونا چاہتے ونرجو القبول من الله تعالى فانه يحتمل ان يكون الفدية واحبہ اس کے اندر یہ احتمال ہے کہ قضا للصلوۃ کے لئے فدیہ واجب ہو کیونکہ فدیہ فی الصوم اگر معلل بالعجز ہو تو پھر عجز فی مسئلہ الصلوة متحقق ہے تو فدیہ جیسے صوم میں واجب تو صلوۃ میں بھی واجب ہو گا اگر تعلیل بالعجز صحیح نہ ہو تو فلا اقل ان يكون آتيا بالمندوب پھر کم از کم اتنا تو ضرور ہے کہ وہ فعل مستحب کر رہا ہے اور امام محمد نے اسی مقام پر کہا ہے نرجو القبول اور اس قسم کے الفاظ مسائل قیاسیہ میں نہیں کہہ جاتے بلکہ صرف احتیاطی مقام میں کہہ جاتے ہیں تو یہ مسلہ احتیاطی ہے قیاسی نہیں ہے ۔ وفي الاضحية اور اضحیہ میں تصدق بعين الشاۃ او قیمتہا کا قول اس لئے ہے لان الاصل في العبادة الخ کيونکہ عبادہ مالیہ میں اصل یہ ہے کہ تصدق بالعین ہونا چاہیے تو اضحیہ بھی تو عبادة
If it is said: Why did you make fidyah obligatory for prayer by qiyas, i.e., on fasting? This is the answer to that objection: You said that such a commanded act, which has no rational equivalent as a worship, its compensation is not performed except by text. So when prayer is missed by an old man, its compensation with fidyah is not correct because fidyah is not a rational equivalent for prayer, and no text has come for prayer; rather, the text of fidyah only came for fasting. So this is a ruling that is not grasped by qiyas, so it should not be analogized to others. So prayer should not be analogized to fasting because qiyas is not applied to rulings that are not grasped by qiyas. As for udhiya, this is the second objection: In udhiya, the shedding of blood apart from the specific days is not known to be a worship. It is unknown whether giving the specific sheep or its value is an equivalent or whether the worship of shedding blood has an equivalent. When its equivalence is not known, why did you make giving the specific or its value obligatory? For the obligation of giving the specific is conjoined to fidyah which is mentioned in 'lam awjibtuhum...' We say: This is the answer. The summary is that the ruling of fidyah in fasting is probable of being caused by inability; i.e., it may be caused by inability. So the old person who is unable to fast, due to that inability, fidyah is made obligatory in place of fasting. Similarly, there is inability for prayer as well. So we said it is obligatory as a precaution. Due to that inability, we also said the obligation of fidyah for prayer. And this meaning is one of precaution. He may come with what is recommended or what is obligatory: so paying fidyah becomes obligatory; if it is not obligatory, then it is recommended. Nevertheless, precaution is that fidyah for prayer should be paid, and we hope for acceptance from Allah. For it is possible that fidyah for prayer is obligatory because if fidyah in fasting is caused by inability, then inability is realized in the issue of prayer, so fidyah would be obligatory in prayer as in fasting. If the determination by inability is not correct, then at least he is doing a recommended act. And Imam Muhammad said at this point: 'We hope for acceptance.' Such words are not said in qiyasi issues; rather, they are said only in precautionary matters. So this is a precautionary issue, not a qiyasi one. And regarding udhiya: the statement of giving the specific sheep or its value is because the principle in financial worship is that giving the specific ('ayn) should be done. So udhiya is also a financial worship.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute. The opponent raises an objection: According to the rule that acts without rational equivalent are not compensated except by text, fidyah (monetary compensation) for prayer cannot be obligatory because fidyah is not a rational equivalent for prayer and no text exists for it (unlike fasting where there is a clear text). Therefore, analogizing prayer to fasting is invalid. Similarly, for udhiya (sacrifice), the opponent argues that the act of shedding blood on specific days is not known to have an equivalent, so why obligate giving the specific animal or its value? The Hanafi response, attributed to Imam Muhammad, is that the ruling on fidyah for fasting is possibly 'mu'allal bil-ajz' (caused by inability). Since the elderly person who is unable to fast is also unable to pray, we apply the same ruling out of precaution (ihtiyat). Even if the causal link (ta'lil) is not certain, at least fidyah becomes a recommended (mandub) act. The use of 'narju al-qabul' (we hope for acceptance) indicates this is a precautionary ruling, not a qiyasi one. Regarding udhiya, the obligation of giving the specific sheep or its value is based on the principle that financial worship (ibada maliyya) must involve giving the actual 'ayn (specific item) unless a text specifies otherwise. Thus, the Hanafis do not rely on qiyas but on a general principle and precaution.

Key Terms
فدية (fidyah): Monetary compensation given by the elderly or terminally ill for missed acts of worship.
تعليل (ta'lil): The process of identifying the underlying cause ('illa) for a ruling.
احتياط (ihtiyat): A legal precaution to ensure compliance with potential obligations.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why is fidyah for prayer considered valid despite the lack of textual evidence?
A) Because qiyas can be applied to all acts of worship without restriction
B) Because fidyah is a rational equivalent for prayer
C) Because the ruling on fidyah in fasting is possibly caused by inability, which also applies to prayer, making it a matter of precaution
D) Because Imam Muhammad personally received a revelation

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul allows extension of rulings in worship by precaution (ihtiyat) when a probable cause is identified, even without strict qiyas.
