The Principle of Ihtiyat in Non-Qiyasi Ibadat
Defending Hanafi application of ihtiyat in fidyah for salah and udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the distinction between qiyas and ihtiyat in Hanafi usul, and apply ihtiyat when qiyas cannot be used.

Core Idea
Ihtiyat (precaution) is a valid basis for rulings in non-qiyasi ibadat, even when qiyas is impossible.

In this lesson, we examine a classical dispute about whether fidyah for salah can be derived by qiyas from sawm, and whether sadaqah of the udhiyah animal after its time is permissible. The Hanafi response reveals that ihtiyat, not qiyas, is the operative principle. This distinction is crucial for understanding how Hanafi jurists derived rulings for cases where direct analogy fails.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
The objector argues that fidyah for salah cannot be derived by qiyas because no text exists for prayer and the substitute is not rationally equivalent. Similarly, requiring sadaqah of the udhiyah goat after its time is invalid because the only known act is shedding blood during the appointed days.
Understand the strict view that non-rational acts of worship cannot be extended except by direct text.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses two examples. For fidyah, they argue based on the common cause of inability ('ajz) using ihtiyat, not qiyas. Even if not obligatory, it is at least recommended. For udhiyah, after the time, they revert to the original principle of sadaqah out of ihtiyat.
Notice the phrase 'we hope for acceptance' (narju al-qabul) used by Imam Muhammad, indicating a precautionary ruling.
3
Distinguish ihtiyat from qiyas
Ihtiyat is based on probability and precaution, not definitive analogy. In Hanafi usul, ihtiyat is a distinct justification separate from qiyas. It is used when direct qiyas fails, based on a probable cause.
The text explicitly says 'this issue is precautionary, not qiyasi'.
4
Apply to the udhiyah case
The original principle in financial worship is sadaqah of the object itself. During udhiyah time, text overrides with shedding blood. After time expires, one may revert to sadaqah of the goat out of ihtiyat, not qiyas.
The derivation is not analogical; it's returning to the original principle when the text-based ruling cannot be performed.
5
Conclude the evidence
The use of ihtiyat does not violate the principle that non-qiyasi rulings cannot be extended by qiyas. The Hanafi school maintains methodological consistency by using a separate tool.
The doubt about whether to follow the text or the original principle is resolved by ihtiyat: choose the more cautious option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لایقاس عليه غيره تو صوم پر غیر صوم یعنی صلوۃ کو قیاس نہ کیا جاتا کیونکہ حکم غیر مدرک بالقیاس میں قیاس نہیں ہوتا اما الاضحية یہ دوسرا اشکال ہے اضحیہ میں اراقة دم ایام مخصوص کے علاوہ قربت ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوا ۔ دلایدری اور یہ بھی معلوم نہیں ہے کہ تصدق بعین الشاہ او بقیمتہا یعنی وہ شاة اضحية بعينها کا صدقہ کرنا یا اوسکی قیمت کا صد قرمل هو مثل کیا اراقة دم کی قربہ مثل ہے یا نہیں جب اس کا مثل ہونا معلوم نہیں ہے تو تم نے تصدق بالعین او بقیمتہ کا وجوب کیوں کیا ہے تور التصدق بالعین کا عطف الفدیہ پر ہے جو لم او جیتیم الغدیر میں مذکور ہے قلنا یہ جواب ہے خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ صوم کے بارہ میں جو فدیہ کا حکم ہے محتمل التعليل بالعجز احتمال رکھتا ہے کہ معلل بالعجز ہو یعنی شیخ فانی جو عاجز عن الصیام ہے اس معجزہ کی بنا پر فدیہ بجائے صیام کے لازم کیا گیا ہے تو میسی عجز عن الصلوۃ بھی ہے فقلنا بالوجوب احتیاطا تو اسی عجز کی بنا پر صلوۃ میں بھی ہم نے قول بوجوب الفدیہ کا کر دیا ہے اور یہ معنی بر احتیاط ہے نیکون آیا بالمندوب اوالو تو فدیہ ادا کرنے میں ادائیگی واجب ہو جائیگی اگر واجب نہ بھی ہو تو مندوب ہو جائیگا پھر بھی احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ فدیہ عن الصلوۃ ہونا چاہتے ونرجو القبول من الله تعالى فانه يحتمل ان يكون الفدية واحبہ اس کے اندر یہ احتمال ہے کہ قضا للصلوۃ کے لئے فدیہ واجب ہو کیونکہ فدیہ فی الصوم اگر معلل بالعجز ہو تو پھر عجز فی مسئلہ الصلوة متحقق ہے تو فدیہ جیسے صوم میں واجب تو صلوۃ میں بھی واجب ہو گا اگر تعلیل بالعجز صحیح نہ ہو تو فلا اقل ان يكون آتيا بالمندوب پھر کم از کم اتنا تو ضرور ہے کہ وہ فعل مستحب کر رہا ہے اور امام محمد نے اسی مقام پر کہا ہے نرجو القبول اور اس قسم کے الفاظ مسائل قیاسیہ میں نہیں کہ جاتے بلکہ صرف احتیاطی مقام میں کہہ جاتے ہیں تو یہ مسلہ احتیاطی ہے قیاسی نہیں ہے ۔ وفي الاضحية اور اضحیہ میں تصدق بعين الشاۃ او قیمتہا کا قول اس لئے ہے لان الاصل في العبادة الخ کيونکہ عبادہ مالیہ میں اصل یہ ہے کہ تصدق بالعین ہونا چاہیے تو اضحیہ بھی تو عبادة مالیہ ہے لہذا اس میں بھی اصل میہی ہو سکتا ہے کہ تصدق بعين الشاۃ ہونا چاہئے الا انه نقل الى الاراقة ليكن ایام تضحیہ میں یہ تصدق بعین انشاۃ منتقل ہو گیا الی الا راقہ یعنی اسی شاہ کو ذبح کر کے خون بہایا جائے تطبییبا للطعام تاکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی جانب سے طعام ضیافہ پاک صاف ہو جائے للعباد یہ ایسے سمجھتے کہ مال صدقہ اوساخ ذنوب ہوتا ہے اس کے اخراج سے دسخ زائل ہو جاتی ہے اور مال سے خبث خارج ہو کر بقیہ مال کو پاک وصاف کر دیتا ہے اسی طرح ایام تضحیہ میں اراقة دم کے ساتھ لحم ضیافہ پاک صاف ہو جائیں گے اور اس سے خیث کا ازالہ ہو جائیگا اور ضیوف کو اللہ تعالیٰ کی جانب سے طیب وطاہر طعام کی ضیافت حاصل ہو اس لئے اضحیہ کے ایام میں اراقۃ واجب ہے لکن لم تعمل لیکن اس تعلیل مظنون یعنی یہ علہ کے عبادہ مالیہ میں اصل تصدق بالعین ہے اس کے ساتھ ہم نے عمل نہیں کیا نی الوقت یعنی وقت تضحیہ میں اس تعلیل پر عمل نہیں کیا حتی لم نقل اس لئے ہم تصدق بالعین کے جواز فی وقت التضحیہ کے قائل نہیں اور چونکہ ایام تضحیہ میں نص بالا راقہ واقع ہے اس لئے معرض نص میں تصدق بالعین والے اصل پر عمل نہیں کیا ان ایام میں تصدق بعین انشاہ جائزہ نہیں ہے وعملنا به بعد الوقت اور وقت تضحیہ جب ختم ہوا اور کسی عذر کی وجہ سے شاہ تضحیہ ذبح نہ ہوسکی تو اس اصل پر یعنی تصدق بعین الثاة پر ہم نے احتیاطا عمل کیا اور قیاسا نہیں ہے لہذا یہ اشکال وارد نہ ہوگا کہ یہ مالا یدرک بالقیاس میں قیاس کرنا لازم آرہا ہے ولهذا یعنی چونکہ بعد الوقت اس اصل تصدق بالعین پر عمل کیا گیا ہے تو جس وقت عام ثانی آیا اور اب تک وہ شاہ باقی ہے تو حکم الى التضحیہ واراقة الدم منتقل نہیں ہو گا ۔ لانه لما احتمل یعنی چونکہ تصدق بالعین اصل ہونیکا احتمال رکھتا تھا اور اس کے ساتھ حکم بھی دیا جا چکا ہے لہم مسجل بالشك تو اس شک پر کہ ممکن ہے کہ اسراقہ اصل ہوا اور اس کا وقت بھی حاصل ہو چکا ہے اس شک کی وجہ سے پہلا حکم باطل نہیں ہوگا ۔
If it is said: Why did you make fidyah obligatory for prayer by qiyas, i.e., on fasting? This is the answer to the objection that you have said: An act of worship whose equivalent is not rationally understood as an act of worship has no qada except by text. When prayer is missed by an aged sheikh, its qada with fidyah is not valid because fidyah is not rationally equivalent to prayer, and no text has come for prayer; rather, the text of fidyah came only for fasting. So this is a ruling not reachable by qiyas, so it should not be analogized to anything else. Thus, other than fasting (i.e., prayer) should not be analogized to fasting, because qiyas does not apply to rulings not reachable by qiyas. As for udhiyah, this is the second objection: in udhiyah, the act of shedding blood (araqa dam) specifically on the appointed days – its being an act of worship is not known. And it is also not known whether charity of the actual goat or its value is similar to the shedding of blood in terms of worship. When its similarity is not known, why did you make obligatory charity of the actual goat or its value? The charity of the actual goat is connected to the fidyah mentioned in the context. We say: This is the answer. Its summary is that the ruling of fidyah in fasting is possibly subject to causation by inability ('ajz), meaning the aged sheikh who is unable to fast, fidyah is made necessary in place of fasting due to this inability. Then similarly, there is inability for prayer, so we said obligation out of precaution (ihtiyat). So due to this inability, we also held the view of obligation of fidyah for prayer. And this meaning is based on precaution. So one comes with either the recommended or obligatory act. If it is not obligatory, then it becomes recommended. Nevertheless, precaution lies in having fidyah for prayer, and we hope for acceptance from Allah. It is possible that the fidyah is obligatory for the qada of prayer, because if fidyah in fasting is based on inability, then inability in the case of prayer is realized, so fidyah becomes obligatory as in fasting. If the causation by inability is not correct, then at least one is coming with the recommended act. And Imam Muhammad said at this place: 'We hope for acceptance.' Such words are not said in qiyasi issues but only in precautionary positions. So this issue is precautionary, not qiyasi. And regarding udhiyah: the view that charity of the actual goat or its value is obligatory is because the principle in financial worship is charity of the actual object. Udhiyah is also a financial worship, so in it the principle could be charity of the actual goat, but it has been transferred to shedding blood during the days of udhiyah, i.e., slaughtering the goat itself and causing blood to flow, to purify the food, so that the food of hospitality becomes pure and clean for the servants from Allah. They understand that charity wealth is the filth of sins; by its removal, dirt is removed, and filth exits from the wealth, purifying the remaining wealth. Similarly, in udhiyah days, with shedding of blood, the meat of hospitality becomes pure and clean, and its filth is removed, and the guests receive pure and clean food from Allah. Thus, shedding blood is obligatory on udhiyah days. But we did not act upon this speculative cause (i.e., the principle of charity of the actual object) – we did not act on it during the time of udhiyah. So we do not allow charity of the actual goat during udhiyah time. And because on udhiyah days, the text for shedding blood exists, in the presence of text we did not act on the principle of charity of the actual object. Charity of the actual goat is not permissible on those days. But we acted on it after the time. And when the udhiyah time ended and due to some excuse the udhiyah goat was not slaughtered, we acted on the principle of charity of the actual goat out of precaution (ihtiyat), not qiyas. So this objection does not arise that qiyas is necessary in a matter not reachable by qiyas. Therefore, because after the time we acted on this principle of charity of the actual goat, when the second year came and the goat still remains, the ruling does not transfer to udhiyah and shedding blood. Because since the principle of charity of the actual goat possibly existed and a ruling has been given accordingly, it is [established] with doubt. So this doubt – that perhaps shedding blood was the principle and its time has passed – does not invalidate the first ruling.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a discussion regarding the application of qiyas in acts of worship. The author (likely the commentator on Al-Tawdih) defends the Hanafi practice of using ihtiyat (precaution) when qiyas cannot be applied. The objector argues that fidyah for salah cannot be derived by qiyas from sawm because the text for fidyah is specific to sawm and salah's substitute is not rationally understood. Hence, applying qiyas would be invalid. The Hanafi response uses two examples: first, fidyah for salah is justified by ihtiyat, not qiyas, based on the common cause of inability ('ajz), and even if it were not obligatory, it is at least recommended. The text emphasizes that Imam Muhammad's phrase 'we hope for acceptance' indicates a precautionary, not qiyasi, ruling. Second, regarding udhiyah, the objector questions how one can require sadaqah of the goat or its value when the only known act is shedding blood. The commentator explains that the original principle in financial worship is sadaqah of the object itself, but for udhiyah, the text (nass) overrides this and prescribes shedding blood during the days. However, after the time of udhiyah expires, if the goat is not slaughtered, one may revert to the original principle of sadaqah out of ihtiyat. Hence, no qiyas is involved.

Key Terms
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary action taken when the ruling is uncertain, based on a probable cause rather than definitive qiyas.
غير مدرك بالقياس (ghayr mudrak bil-qiyas): A ruling that cannot be rationally deduced through analogy because its basis is not rationally understood (e.g., acts of worship whose modality is only known by text).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the text, why is fidyah for salah permitted despite the absence of direct text?
A) Because qiyas from fasting is valid.
B) Because of ihtiyat based on the common cause of inability.
C) Because the text for fasting implicitly includes prayer.
D) Because fidyah is obligatory in all cases of missed worship.

Key Takeaway
Ihtiyat is a valid Hanafi usul tool for deriving rulings in ibadat when qiyas is impossible, based on probability and precaution.

Incomplete Delivery and Possession: The Hanafi Dispute
Analyzing incomplete delivery and its effect on possession in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on incomplete delivery and identify the qiyas used by Abu Hanifa, and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's view based on the concept of defect.

Core Idea
Incomplete delivery annuls possession; liability attaches only upon complete transfer.

This passage examines a key dispute within the Hanafi school concerning the effect of defects or pending liabilities on possession after a sale. Abu Hanifa holds that if the sold item is subject to a crime that leads to its destruction, the original delivery is incomplete and possession is void. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider such a condition merely a defect that does not prevent possession but only allows compensation for the diminution. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the Hanafi criteria for valid possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and the point of dispute
The passage discusses a sold slave who is subject to a crime (جنایت) and dies due to that crime. The central question is whether the buyer's possession (قبض) is valid and complete.
The dispute affects who bears the loss: buyer or seller.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) and its proof
Abu Hanifa rules that the possession is annulled because the delivery was incomplete; the slave was not free from liability. The proof is an analogy (qiyas) to incomplete delivery: since the item is still encumbered by liability, it is as if no proper delivery occurred.
Key principle: adā’ qāṣir does not transfer liability.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its proof
The two companions consider the crime as a defect (عیب) that does not prevent possession. They analogize to the case of paying a debt with counterfeit dirhams unknowingly accepted; possession is complete despite the defect.
They allow recourse only for the defect's reduction in value, not full annulment.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the slave dies, Abu Hanifa allows the buyer to recover the full price, while the Sahibayn only allow recovery of the difference due to the defect. The same principle applies to a usurped animal that becomes pregnant and dies.
The dispute extends to other cases involving pending liability.
5
Evaluate the istinbat path
The disagreement stems from whether the crime is considered integral to the item's liability (Abu Hanifa) or separable as a defect (Sahibayn). The qiyas used by each side reflects different categorizations of the condition.
This illustrates how the definition of qabḍ and adā’ affects rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متھی تو یہ بھی ادائے قاصر ہے حتى اذا ملك بذلك السبب یہ اس کے قاصر ہونے پر تفریح ہے اگر یہ مبیع مشغول بالجنایت اسی جنایت میں قتل ہو کر ہلاک ہوا تو انتقض القبض عند ابي حنيفه تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ قبض باطل ہو جائیگی کان المشترى لم يقبض لهذا مشتری کل شمن کار جوع کرے گا عن البائع وعندهما هذا عیب اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ ایک عیب ہے اور عیب تمامیہ تسلیم اور قبض سے مانع نہیں ہوتا لہذا مشتری کی قبض تام ہو چکی ہے كاداء الزيوف جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے قرضہ میں قرض خواہ کو دراہم زیوف ادا کرتا ہے اور صاحب الحق کو علم نہیں ہوتا تو یہ قبض تام ہو جاتی ہے حتى لو هلك عنده اگر یہ عبد مشغول مشتری کے ہاں بلاک ہوا تو اس کا حق باطل ہو جائیگا رجوع بالثمن کلہا تو نہیں کر سکتا البتہ رجوع بالنقصان ہوگا اور اسی طرح اختلاف ہو گا جارہ یہ منصوبہ میں جو غاصب کے ہاں حاملہ ہوئی ہے پھر اس نے واپس کی ہے اور مالک کے ہاں اسی سبب سے ہلاک ہوئی ہے تو امام کے نزدیک تمام قیمت کی ضمان مناصب پر لازم ہوگی ۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک ضمان نہیں ہوگی۔
This is also incomplete delivery. ... If this slave, subject to a crime, is killed in that crime and dies, then the possession is annulled according to Abu Hanifa, so this possession becomes void, as if the buyer did not take possession. ... According to the two companions, this is a defect, and a defect does not prevent complete delivery and possession, so the buyer's possession is complete. ... Similarly, there will be a dispute in the case of the usurped (animal) that became pregnant with the usurper, then he returned it, and it died with the owner due to that same cause. According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), full value is guaranteed to the usurper; according to the two companions, there is no guarantee.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of incomplete delivery (ادائے قاصر) and its effect on possession (قبض). The scenario is a sale of a slave who is subject to a crime. If the slave dies due to that crime, Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer's possession is annulled because the delivery was incomplete (the slave was not free from liability). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the condition a defect (عیب), which does not prevent complete possession. The example of counterfeit dirhams (دراہم زیوف) is given to illustrate that if the creditor unknowingly accepts counterfeit coins, possession is complete. The same principle applies to a usurped animal that becomes pregnant and dies: Abu Hanifa holds the usurper liable for full value, while the two companions say no liability.

Key Terms
ادائے قاصر (adā’ qāṣir): Delivery that is incomplete due to a defect or pending liability, not transferring full possession.
قبض (qabḍ): Possession or taking delivery of the sold item, which transfers liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a purchased slave is subject to a crime and dies, what happens to the buyer's possession?
A) The possession is complete and the buyer bears the loss.
B) The possession is annulled and the buyer can recover the full price.
C) The possession is valid but the buyer can only claim a reduction.
D) The possession is void and the buyer loses all rights.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between complete and incomplete delivery hinges on whether the item is free from pending liabilities; a defect alone does not annul possession but only allows recourse for the diminution.

Tadakhul of Penalties: The Case of Cutting Hand Then Killing
Hanafi analysis of whether qisas for hand and life combine, with evidence from tadakhul and Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument for tadakhul in penalties by distinguishing between penalty for the act and penalty for the locus, and apply the Quranic analogy to a similar case.

Core Idea
Tadakhul only applies to penalties for the same locus, not to separate acts — thus cutting and killing each retain their own qisas.

This passage delves into a critical usul principle: when do multiple penalties merge? Using the case of a murderer who first cuts off a hand then kills, the Hanafi school defends the guardian's right to exact qisas for both acts. The key lies in distinguishing between a penalty for the locus (jazā' al-mahall) and a penalty for the act (jazā' al-fi'l). We will trace the dispute with the Sahibayn and analyze the Quranic proof that killing can erase, not complete, the cut's effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The legal question is whether qisas for cutting the hand is still available after the murderer kills the victim.
The answer depends on whether cutting and killing are separate crimes or one continuous act.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the guardian can choose to exact qisas for both (hand then life) or only life. The basis is that tadakhul only occurs in penalties for the same locus, not for separate acts.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's argument
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that the cut spread (sarayat) and the killing completes the effect, making it one crime. Therefore, only qisas for life is allowed.
4
Examine the Hanafi counter-argument
The Hanafi response: killing can erase the cut's effect, as shown by the Quranic verse: slaughtering a mauled animal removes its prohibition. Thus, the killing does not complete but nullifies the cut's effect.
The verse is Quran 5:3 (part).
5
Distinguish between penalty for act and penalty for locus
Apply the principle: penalties for separate acts remain separate (each act has its own qisas). Tadakhul only applies when multiple penalties are due for harm to the same locus (e.g., head wound and hair destruction).
This distinction is central to the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقضاء بمثل معقول اما کامل یعنی جو مثل صورة و معنی ہو اس کو فوت شدہ شئی کے عوض دیا جائے تو یہ قضاء بمثل کامل قضاء کامل ہوگی واما قاصر یا قاصر ہوگی جیسے اس شئی کی قیمت ادا کرنا اس وقت جب اس کی مثل منقطع ہو چکی ہے یا سرے سے اس کی مثل صوری تھی ہی نہیں چونکہ مثل صوری سے عجز ہو چکا ہے اس لئے اس کا حق فی الصورة فوت ہو چکا ہے اب صرف مثل معنوی باقی ہے وہ ہے قیمت لہذا یہی ادا کی جائے گی ۔ فلا يجب القاصر قاصر واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ مگر اس وقت جب کامل سے عجز ہو ۔ نفی قطع اليد ثم القتل خیر الولی یعنی ایک شخص نے کسی انسان کا ہاتھ کاٹا پھر اس کے بعد اسے قتل کر دیا تو ولی مقتول کو اختیار ہو گا چاہے تو پہلے قاتل کا قطع ید کرے پھر اسے قتل کرے وھو مثل کامل یہ ہے مثل کامل اگر ولی مقتول چاہے تو صرف قتل کرے دھو قاصر یہ قاصر ہے وعندهما لا يقطع اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت مذکورہ میں ولی مقتول کو قطع ید کا اختیار نہیں ہے لانه انما یقتی کیونکہ قصاص بالقطع اسوقت ہوتا ہے جب یہ واضح ہو جائے کہ قطع نے سرایت نہیں کی اور مفضی الی الموت نہیں ہوئی ۔ فاذا افضى اليه جنب یہ قطع سرایت کر کے مفضی الی القتل ہو جائے تو اس وقت موجب قطع موجب قتل میں داخل ہو جاتا ہے اور موجب سے مراد اس مقام میں وہی کشتی ہے جو قتل و قطع کے ساتھ واجب ہوتا ہے یعنی قصاص تو قصاص ید قصاص نفس میں درج ہو جائیگا۔ اذا القتل اتم موجب القطع اور موجب سے مراد یہاں اثر حاصل بالقطع ہے یعنی قطع کے ساتھ جو اثر ثابت ہوتا یعنی سرایت مفضيته الى القتل تو اس قتل نے جو بعد القطع واقع ہوا اثر قطع کو اس محل قطع میں تمام کر دیا ہے یعنی ابلاک نفس گویا کہ قطع پھر قتل یہ ایسے ہو جائیگا جیسے قطع سرایت معنی الی القتل ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں یہ جنایت واحدہ ہوگی - فصار كما اذا قتله بضربات یہ ایسے ہو جیسے قاتل مقتول کو ضربات متعددہ کے ساتھ قتل کرتا ہے تو اس صورۃ میں ضربات کا قصاص نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صرف قصاص نفس یعنی قتل ہوتا ہے تو اسی طرح یہاں بھی قصاص قطع نہیں ہو گا صرف قصاص نفس یعنی قتل ہوگا ۔ تلنا هذا من حيث المعنی یعنی جو یہ کہا گیا ہے کہ قتل نے اثر قطع کو متمتم کر دیا تو یہ جنایتہ واحدہ ہے لہذا ان کا موجب اور مقتضا ایک ہونا چاہیے یہ استحداد من حیث المعنی ہے من حیث الصورة نہیں ، اما من حيث الصورة في جزاء الفعل فلا يعنى من حيث الصورة جو جزائے فعل ہونی چاہئے اس میں اتحاد نہیں فعل یعنی قطع اور قتل صورۃ الگ الگ اور متعدد فعل ہیں ما هو جزاء الفعل هو القصاص لہذا ہر فعل کا الگ الگ قصاص ہونا چاہیئے وانما يدخل في جزاء المحل یعنی جزاء محل میں تداخل ہوتا ہے کہ ضمان جزر ضمان کل میں داخل ہو جاتی ہے جہاں جزاء محل ہو اور تین افعل میں ایسے نہیں ہوتا كا يدخل ارش الموضحة في دية الشعريه تداخل في جزاء المحل کی مثال ہے صورۃ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی شخص نے ایک انسان کو سر میں زخم موضحہ لگایا جس کے اثر سے سر نے بال تباہ ہو گئے جن کے دوبارہ اُگنے کی توقع بھی نہیں ہے چونکہ محل ایک ہے لہذا جو دیت شعر ہے موضحہ کا تاوان اسی میں متداخل ہو جائیں گے صرف دیت شعر لازم ہوگی ارش موضحہ واجب نہیں ہوگی هذ الان الدية عزاء المحل کیونکہ دیۃ الشعر جزاء محل ہے تو ارش موضحہ اس میں متداخل ہو جائیگی والقتل قد يمحو اثر القطع یہ اس کا جواب ہے جو صاحبین نے کہا تھا کہ قتل متمم ہے اثر قطع کا یعنی قطع سرایت کر کے قتل تک مفضی ہو جاتی ہے تو قتل بعد القطع نے اُس اثر کو تمامیتہ تک پہونچا دیا ہے خلاصہ جواب یہ یہ ہے کہ قتل کبھی اثر قطع کی تمیم کے بجائے اس کے اثر کو محو کر دیتا ہے اور مٹا دیتا ہے کیونکہ قتل کے ساتھ محل ہی فوت ہو گیا فوات محل کے ساتھ قطع کا اتمام اور اس کی سرایت ممکن ہی نہیں رہی لہذا اتمام کیسے متصور ہو سکتا ہے قال الله تعالى وما اكل السبع الدما ذكيتم بہ ایک مثال ہے اس کی کہ قتل قطع کے اثر کو مٹا دیتا ہے جیسے ایک شاہ کو درندے نے زخمی کیا اور اس کا گوشت کاٹ کر کھایا تو اس کی شریعت نے حرمت قائم کر دی اگر یہی زخم اور قطع لحم مفضی الی الموت ہو جائے الاماز کیتیم کا استثناء بتلا رہا ہے کہ اگر اسی حالت میں شاہ کی حیات کچھ باقی ہو ذکات شرعیہ کے ساتھ ذبح کر لی جائے تو یہ شاہ حلال ہے تو دیکھئے کہ اس قتل نے جو بصورۃ زکوۃ شرعیہ ہوا ہے قطع اور جرح کے حکم کو مٹا دیا ہے اگر اسی جرح سے مرتی تو حرام تھی قتل زکاتی نے اس اثر کو
And judgment by equivalent (qadā' bi'l-mithl) is either complete (kāmil) or defective (qāṣir). A complete equivalent is that which matches in form and meaning. A defective equivalent is like paying its value when its physical equivalent has ceased or never existed. Since physical equivalent is impossible, his right in form is lost; only the equivalent in meaning remains, which is value, so that is paid. Defective is not obligatory except when complete is impossible. The case of cutting off the hand then killing: the guardian of the slain has the option: if he wishes, he may first cut off the murderer's hand then kill him – that is complete equivalent; if he wishes only to kill – that is defective. And according to them (the two Companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not cut off the hand, because qisas for cutting is only when it is clear that the cut did not spread and did not lead to death. If it led to death, then the cause of the cut enters into the cause of killing – meaning the qisas for the hand merges into the qisas for life. Because the killing completes the effect of the cut: the cut lead to death, so the post-cut killing completes the effect – as if the cutting spread to death, making it one crime – like killing by multiple blows: qisas for blows is not applied, only qisas for life. Similarly here, only qisas for life applies. We say: this is from the perspective of meaning, not form. Regarding the form of the penalty, there is no unity: the acts (cutting and killing) are separate acts; the penalty for each act should be separate. However, tadakhul (interlocking) occurs in the penalty of the locus (jazā' al-mahall), so that the compensation for a part enters the compensation for the whole. This does not happen in separate acts. For example, the compensation for a head wound (arsh al-muḍiḥah) enters into the blood money for hair (diyat al-sha'r) in the case where someone inflicts a head wound that destroys hair that will not regrow: because the locus is one, the blood money for hair is the penalty for the locus, so the arsh merges into it. And killing may erase the effect of cutting: this is the response to the Sahibayn who said that killing completes the cut's effect. The summary is that killing sometimes erases the effect rather than completing it, because the locus itself is destroyed, so completion is impossible. Allah says: '…and what the beast of prey has eaten, except what you slaughter.' This is an example that killing erases the effect of cutting: a sheep mauled by a predator is prohibited, but if it is slaughtered while alive, it becomes lawful. So the slaughter (killing) removes the ruling of the injury; similarly, here the killing removes the effect of the cut.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage examines the concept of judgment by equivalent (qaḍā' bi'l-mithl) and its application in the case of an offender who first cuts off a person's hand and then kills him. The Hanafi position (attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa) gives the guardian a choice: either to exact qisas for both the hand and the life (complete equivalent) or only for the life (defective equivalent). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, arguing that qisas for the hand is not permitted because the cut is subsumed in the killing; the cut's effect is completed by the death, making the act a single crime. The commentator then defends the Hanafi view by distinguishing between tadakhul in the penalty for the locus (jazā' al-mahall) and tadakhul in separate acts. He provides an example: if someone inflicts a head wound (muḍiḥah) that destroys the hair (sha'r) permanently, the blood money for the hair (diyat al-sha'r) covers the compensation, and the arsh for the wound merges into it because the locus is one. However, cutting and killing are separate acts, so their penalties should remain separate. The final argument counters the Sahibayn's view that killing completes the cut's effect; rather, killing can erase the effect, as proven by the Quranic verse about slaughtering a mauled animal: the slaughter (killing) removes the prohibition caused by the mauling. Thus, the cut's effect is nullified, not completed. This passage illustrates a Hanafi usul principle of tadakhul (interlocking of compensations) and its limits.

Key Terms
قضاء بمثل (qaḍā' bi'l-mithl): Judgment by equivalent compensation; if exact equivalent exists (in form and meaning), it is complete (kāmil); if only in meaning (e.g., value), it is defective (qāṣir).
تداخل (tadākhul): Interlocking of compensations: when multiple penalties are due for acts affecting the same locus, the lesser penalty merges into the greater.
جزاء المحل (jazā' al-mahall): The compensation due for the locus (the body part or thing) itself, as opposed to compensation for a specific act. Example: diyat al-sha'r (blood money for hair) covers arsh al-muḍiḥah (compensation for head wound) when the hair is destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the basis for the guardian's option to exact qisas for both cutting and killing?
A) The Quranic verse commands qisas for both.
B) Tadakhul in the penalty for the locus.
C) The Sahibayn's agreement.
D) The acts are separate and tadakhul does not apply to separate acts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows separate qisas for cutting and killing because tadakhul only merges penalties for the same locus, not for distinct acts.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Are Benefits Valuable? The Hanafi Refutation of Shafi‘i Analogies
Refuting Shafi‘i analogies by distinguishing inherent value from contractual concessions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mutaqawwam, identify why benefits are not mutaqawwam, and evaluate the Shafi‘i analogies from ijarah and nikah using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Benefits are not valuable because they lack permanence and cannot be preserved; their valuation in contracts is an exception, not a rule.

This lesson delves into a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools: are benefits (manafi‘) considered valuable property (mutaqawwam)? The Hanafi school holds that benefits are mere accidents (a‘rad) that cannot be preserved, hence not valuable. The Shafi‘i school counters that benefits are clearly exchanged in valid contracts like ijarah and nikah, proving their value. We will walk through the Hanafi response, which distinguishes between inherent value and value arising from exceptional concessions.

Guided Path
1
Define mutaqawwam and identify its conditions
Start with the Hanafi definition: a thing is mutaqawwam if it can be preserved (ihraz) and has permanence (baqa‘). Determine why benefits fail these conditions.
Benefits are accidents; accidents do not last.
2
Analyze the Shafi‘i objection from ijarah
The Shafi‘i argues that ijarah (hire) is valid on benefits, so benefits must be valuable. Follow the Hanafi response: the contract is on the substance (‘ayn), not the benefit directly; the substance substitutes for the benefit.
The lessee uses the substance, not a separate 'benefit'.
3
Analyze the Shafi‘i objection from nikah
The Shafi‘i cites Quran 4:24 and the permissibility of mahr in the form of service. Understand the Hanafi response: this is a concession (rukhsa) based on mutual consent, contrary to qiyas, and not extendable to ghasp.
Mutual consent creates value where none exists inherently.
4
Evaluate the two analogies (qiyas) used by Shafi‘i
The text refutes two analogies: (1) analogizing valuation in ghasp to valuation in contracts (the latter is khilaf al-qiyas), and (2) analogizing exchange for wealth in ghasp to exchange in khul‘ (difference: mutual consent).
A matter that is itself contrary to qiyas cannot serve as an asl for qiyas.
5
Apply the ruling to a subsidiary case (tafri‘)
See how the principle applies to witnesses testifying about forgiveness of qisas. The ruling shows that rights without measurable value cannot be adjudicated without text.
This illustrates the broader principle: no compensation without explicit Shari‘ah valuation.

یعنی جس شی کا احراز نہیں ہو سکتا وہ غیر متقوم ہوتی ہیں یعنی ان کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی ۔ احراز کا معنی ہے ایک شی محفوظ کرنا اور ذخیرہ کرنا تا کہ بوقت ضرورت کام میں لائی جائے ولا احراز بلا بقاء جوشی باقی نہیں رہ سکتی اس کا احراز نہیں ہو سکتا منافع تو اعراض ہیں دلا بقا اللہ عراض اور اراض کے لئے بقا نہیں ہے اس لئے منافع کی ضمان نہیں ہوگی اور نص اس میں وارد نہیں ہے لہنا قیاس کے ساتھ اثرات ضمان نہیں ان منافع پر عقد اجارہ کیسے وارد ہوتا ہے دانہ کا اجارہ پر لینا تاکہ اس پر سواری اختیار کرے گا سکونت کی خاطر دار اجارہ پر لینا یہ تمام عقود اجارہ صحیح ہیں پھر یہ منافع پر کیسے صحیح ہیں ۔ قلنا باقامة العين مقامها جواب یہ کرین اشیاء کو قائم مقام منافع کے قرار دیدیا جاتا جب متاجر نے دار پر قبضہ کر لیا یا دابہ پر تو پس یہی اشیاء جو قابل منافع میں یہ قائمقام منافع کے ہو جاتے ہیں خان قبل هي في العقد مال متقوم اس سوال کے اندر خود منافع کو بلا قائمقام اشیاء کے متقوم قرار دینے کی کوشش ہے خلاصہ سوالی یہ کہ عقد میں خود منافع مال متقوم ہیں لتقدمها في عقد النكاح عقد نکاح میں منافع متقوم ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اور شریعت میں عقد نکاح میں مال متقوم دینا ہوتا ہے لان ابتغاء البضع وهو النكاح لا يجوز الا بالمال المتقوم كما قال الله تعالى ان تبتغوا باموالكم ويجوز ابتغاء البضع بمنفعة الاجازة اور ابتغاء يضع یعنی نکاح منفعہ اجارہ کے عرض کرنا بھی صحیح ہے۔ مثلا ایک شخص کسی عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کرتا ہے اور حق المہر میں متعین کرتا ہے کہ میریہ عبد یا جاریستہ سال بھر تیری خدمت کرے گی تو یہ منفعت اجارہ عقد نکاح میں مال متقوم ہو رہا ہے کیونکہ ابتغاء بضع تو بالمال تھا تو معلوم ہوا کہ منافع مال متقوم ہیں فتکون کی نفعا تو فی حد ذا تہا بھی یہ متقوم ہوں گے کیونکہ جوشنی فی حد ذاتها متقوم نہ ہو ورود عقد کے ساتھ وہ متقوم نہیں ہو سکتی دلان تقومها ليس لاحتياج العقد اليه هنا دليل آخر على قوله فتكون في نفسها كذلك يعنى منافع كافى حد ذاتها متقوم ہونے پر سے دوسری دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کا ان منافع کا تقوم اس بنا پر نہیں ہے کہ عقدان کے تقوم کی طرف محتاج ہے اس بات کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے دلیل پیش کی لان العقد قد يصح بدونه عقد کبھی بدون المال المتقوم صحیح ہوتا ہے کا لخلع فات منافع البضع الأکیونکہ منافع بضع کے جب عقد نکاح سے خارج ہوتے ہیں تو غیر متقوم ہوتے ہیں وان كانت متقدمة اگر متقوم تھے جس وقت داخل فی عقد النکاح ہو رہے تھے لیکن طلاق کے وقت ان کی قیمت نہیں ہوئی نمع انها باوجود اس بات کے کہ حالتہ خروج میں متقوم نہیں تھے لیکن پھر بھی ان کا مقابلہ بالمال عقد خلع میں صحیح ہے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عقد ان کے تقوم کی طرف محتاج نہیں ہے ۔ تتقو معانی العقد پس منافع کا تقوم ضرورة عقد کی بنا پر نہ ہوا تو اس کے باوجود عقد میں ان کا تقوم ثابت ہے تو یہ دلیل ہے کہ فی حد ذاتها منافع متقوم ہیں ۔ تلنا تقومہا یہ جواب ہے اس کا جو دلیل اول میں کہا تھا کہ جو شنی متقوم نہ ہو ورود عقدے ساتھ متقوم نہیں ہو جاتی تو یہ جواب بصورت منع ہے ۔ بل بصیرتى العقد متقدما بلکہ عقد میں ہی یہ متقوم ہو جاتے ہیں بالرضاء اسی برضاء الطرفين بخلاف القیاس ان کا رضا کے ساتھ عقد میں متقوم ہونا خلاف قیاس ہے کیونکہ مال متقوم وہی ہو سکتا جس میں احراز ہو جب منافع میں احراز نہیں ہو سکتا عقلاً یہ مال متقوم نہیں ہو سکتا تو عقد میں ان کا برضاء فریقین متقوم ہونا خلاف قیاس ہے فلایقاس علیہ ان پر آگے قیاس نہیں ہو سکتا۔ شمل معنیین اس عبارت کے دو معنی ہو سکتے ہیں ایک یہ کہ غصب میں منافع کو متقوم قرار دینا اس کا قیاس اس پر نہیں ہو سکتا کہ عقد میں یہ متقوم ہیں کیونکہ عقد میں ان کا متقوم ہونا خلاف قیاس ہے غیر قیاسی امر پر قیاس نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ والثاني انه لا يقاس الخ دوسرا معنی یہ ہے کہ غصب میں منافع کو مقابل مال قرار دینا اس کو قیاس نہیں کیا جاسکتا اس پر کے عقد میں منافع مقابل مال ہیں ۔ دوسرا معنی خود ان کے دعوی کو رد کر رہا ہے۔ دعوی ان کا یہ تھا کہ غصب میں منافع کا مقابل بالمال ہونا صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ عقد میں مقابل مال ہوتے ہیں پہلے معنی کے لحاظ سے ان کے تقوم في الغصب کو قیاس کرنا على التقوم في العقد کو رد کر رہا ہے لهذا المعنی یعنی چونکہ تقوم في العقد خلاف قياس لهذا تقوم المنافع في الغصب کو قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں قیاس بالمعنی الاول کے بطلان پر یہ دلیل ہوئی والفارق ايضا وهوالرضا یہ قیاس بالمعنی الثانی یعنی مقابلة المنافع بالمال في الغصب کو قیاس کرنا على مقابلة المنافع بالمال في عقد الخلع کہ ان کے مابین رضا مندی فارق ہے کہ ضلع میں رضاء فریقین موجود ہے غصب میں ایسے نہیں ہے یہ دلیل ہے قیاس بالمعنی الثانی کے بطلان پر ولا يضمن الشاهد الخ هذا تفریع یہ جو کہا کہ جس شئی کی مثل معقول نہ ہو تو اس کی قضا بغیر نص من الشارع کے نہیں ہو سکتی یہ اسی پر تفریح ہے صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دو شاہدوں نے قاضی کے سامنے شھادۃ دی کہ ولی معقول نے قصاص معاف کر دیا ہے قاضی نے اس شھادۃ کی وجہ سے فیصلہ بالعفو صادر کر دیا پھر یہ
That is, a thing which cannot be preserved (ihraz) is non-valuable (ghayr mutaqawwam), i.e. it has no value. Ihraz means to protect and store a thing so that it can be used when needed. And there is no preservation without permanence. A thing that cannot remain cannot be preserved. Benefits (manafi‘) are accidents (a‘rad). There is no permanence for accidents. Therefore, there will be no guarantee (daman) for benefits, and no text (nass) is reported regarding this. So by analogy (qiyas) they cannot be guaranteed. According to Imam Shafi‘i, they are guaranteed with wealth. According to him, benefits are valuable (mutaqawwam). So from his side there is this objection which the author has presented: 'If it is said: How does the contract occur upon them?' i.e. if benefits are not valuable, then how does a contract of ijarah occur upon those benefits? Renting a beast for riding, renting a house for dwelling – all these ijarah contracts are valid. Then how are they valid upon benefits? We say: By making the substance (ayn) stand in their place. The answer is that we place things as substitutes for benefits. When the lessor takes possession of the house or the beast, then these things become substitutes for the benefits. As if before (the contract) they were, in the contract, valuable property (mal mutaqawwam). In this question, there is an attempt to make the benefits themselves valuable without the substitute things. The summary of the question is that in the contract, the benefits themselves are valuable property, because they are presented (muqaddam) in the contract of nikah. In the contract of nikah, benefits become valuable. And in Shari‘ah, in the contract of nikah, valuable property must be given, because seeking the pudendum (al-bud‘), i.e. marriage, is not permissible except with valuable property, as Allah said: 'that you seek them with your wealth' (Quran 4:24). And it is permissible to seek the pudendum with the benefit of ijarah. That is, marriage by offering the benefit of ijarah is also valid. For example, a man marries a woman and specifies as mahr that his slave girl will serve her for one year. So this benefit of ijarah becomes valuable property in the marriage contract, because seeking the pudendum was with wealth. So it becomes known that benefits are valuable property. Then if they are beneficial, then in themselves too they will be valuable, because a thing that is not valuable in itself cannot become valuable by the occurrence of a contract. There is another evidence for his statement that they are in themselves valuable: The summary is that the valuation (taqawwum) of these benefits is not because the contract is needful of their valuation. To prove this point he presented an evidence: because the contract may be valid without it. For example, khul‘. When the benefits of the pudendum exit from the marriage contract, they are non-valuable, even if they were valuable when they were included in the marriage contract. But at the time of divorce, they have no value. Yet, despite the fact that at the time of exit they were not valuable, still their exchange for wealth in the contract of khul‘ is valid. So from this it becomes known that the contract is not needful of their valuation. The valuation of the contract... So the valuation of benefits did not occur by necessity of the contract. Despite that, their valuation is established in the contract. So this is evidence that in themselves benefits are valuable. Then (the author says): 'His statement (that they become valuable) is the answer to what he said in the first evidence: that a thing that is not valuable does not become valuable by the occurrence of a contract.' This answer is in the form of prevention (man‘). Rather, they become valuable at the onset of the contract, by mutual consent, contrary to analogy (qiyas). Their becoming valuable in the contract by consent is contrary to analogy, because valuable property is only that which can be preserved. When benefits cannot be preserved rationally, they cannot be valuable property. So their becoming valuable in the contract by mutual consent is contrary to analogy. Therefore, nothing can be analogized to it. This phrase can have two meanings. One: That making benefits valuable in ghasp cannot be analogized to their being valuable in the contract, because their being valuable in the contract is contrary to analogy; a non-analogical matter cannot be analogized. Second: That making benefits exchangeable for wealth in ghasp cannot be analogized to making benefits exchangeable for wealth in the contract of khul‘. The second meaning refutes their claim. Their claim was that benefits being exchangeable for wealth in ghasp is correct because they are exchangeable for wealth in contracts. According to the first meaning, it refutes analogizing their valuation in ghasp to their valuation in the contract. For this meaning: Since valuation in the contract is contrary to analogy, therefore analogizing valuation of benefits in ghasp is not correct. This is evidence for the invalidity of the first qiyas. And the differentiator (al-fariq) is also mutual consent. This is evidence for the invalidity of the second qiyas, i.e. analogizing the exchange of benefits for wealth in ghasp to their exchange for wealth in khul‘ – because in khul‘ there is mutual consent, whereas in ghasp there is none. And (the statement) 'And the witness is not liable...' etc. is a subdivision (tafri‘). This is a subdivision of what was said: That a thing whose like is not rationally conceivable cannot be decided without a text from the Lawgiver. The case is: Two witnesses testified before the judge that the guardian (wali) of the victim had forgiven the qisas. The judge, based on this testimony, issued a verdict of forgiveness. Then...
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute defending the Hanafi position that benefits (manafi‘) are not inherently valuable (mutaqawwam) and thus cannot be guaranteed (daman) in cases of unlawful seizure (ghasp). The author begins by defining mutaqawwam: a thing must be capable of preservation (ihraz), which requires permanence. Benefits, being accidents (a‘rad), lack permanence, so they are not valuable. No explicit text (nass) supports guaranteeing them, and analogy (qiyas) cannot establish such a ruling. The Shafi‘i objection is then presented: if benefits are not valuable, how can contracts of ijarah (hire/lease) be valid, since they are exchanged for benefits? The Hanafi response is that in such contracts, the substance of the thing (the ‘ayn) is placed as a substitute for the benefit; the contract is not on the benefit itself but on the object, with the benefit following. The object itself is valuable and possessed. The Shafi‘i further argues that benefits are valuable in the contract of nikah (marriage), as the wife's mahr is often a benefit (e.g., service). The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes: in nikah, the benefit becomes valuable by necessity of the contract, but that is a concession (rukhsa) contrary to qiyas, established by the Quranic verse and mutual consent. It is not a recognition of inherent value. The proof is from khul‘: even when the benefits of the pudendum are no longer in the contract (after divorce), they can still be exchanged for wealth in khul‘, showing that the contract itself does not require their valuation. Therefore, their valuation in nikah is a special case, not based on intrinsic value. The author then refutes two analogies: (1) analogizing the valuation of benefits in ghasp to their valuation in contracts (since the latter is contrary to qiyas, it cannot be a basis for qiyas), and (2) analogizing the exchange of benefits for wealth in ghasp to such exchange in khul‘ (the differentiator is mutual consent – present in khul‘, absent in ghasp). The passage ends with a subsidiary application (tafri‘): if two witnesses testify that a guardian has forgiven qisas, and the judge rules based on that, the ruling stands; but if the witnesses are false, they are not liable because benefits (like the right to qisas?) are not known to be valuable? The exact connection is that the right to qisas is not a fixed wealth (mal) until it is established. This illustrates the principle that matters without a known measurable value cannot be adjudicated without scriptural text.

Key Terms
منافع (manafi‘): Benefits, usufructs, i.e. the utility derived from a thing, such as riding, dwelling, or service.
متقوم (mutaqawwam): Having a recognized value in Shari‘ah, such that its destruction or seizure entails compensation (daman). Essential characteristics: ihraz (safekeeping) and baqa‘ (permanence).
اعراض (a‘rad): Accidental qualities that are non-permanent, such as color, taste, and also usufructs (manafi‘). They do not have independent existence.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease, whereby the benefit (manfa‘ah) of an asset is transferred to the lessee in exchange for rent (ujrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the ruling on guaranteeing (daman) the value of benefits (manafi‘) in cases of unlawful seizure (ghasp)?
A) They must be compensated with the like (misl) or value (qimah) because they are considered property in contracts.
B) No guarantee is payable because benefits are not permanent enough to be preserved, so they are not mutaqawwam.
C) Guarantee is payable only if the benefits were explicitly specified in a prior contract.
D) The guarantee is half of the benefit's value, by analogy to the compensation for destroying a right (haqq).

Key Takeaway
Benefits are not inherently valuable property because they lack permanence and preservation; their valuation in contracts is an exception, not a rule, and cannot be extended to ghasp via qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Principle of Non-Compensation for Rights Without Known Equivalent
Expansion of the rule on non-compensable rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a right without a known equivalent cannot be compensated by property, and distinguish between cases where analogy (qiyas) is valid vs. invalid.

Core Idea
A right without a known equivalent cannot be monetarily compensated – the rule forbids qiyas when the mithl is unknown.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary establishes a key boundary: some rights, like the right to exact qisas (retaliation), have no known equivalent in property. Consequently, monetary compensation (daman) cannot be imposed as a substitute. The commentary explores the implications through three examples: usufruct in contracts, retraction of witnesses in a qisas case, and an unspecified slave as dower. Understanding this rule deepens your grasp of when analogy is permissible and when istihsan (juristic preference) overrides it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Locate the statement that a thing with no known equivalent (mithl ma'qul) cannot be compensated by property without explicit text. This is the foundational principle of the lesson.
The rule is implicitly stated: 'لان استيفاء القصاص معنى لا مثل له' – exacting qisas is a meaning with no equivalent.
2
Trace the application in the qisas case
Follow the reasoning: witnesses retract their testimony that the guardian pardoned qisas. The judge had already ruled. Why are the witnesses not liable? Because the right they wasted (qisas) has no known property equivalent.
The text explicitly says property cannot substitute for the meaning of qisas.
3
Contrast with usufruct in contracts
The passage earlier discusses usufruct (manafi') in a khul' contract. Usufruct becomes valuable through mutual consent (istihsan), even though rationally it cannot be possessed. This is an exception that cannot be analogized to other contexts (e.g., usurpation).
This step shows the limit of analogy: a ruling based on istihsan is not extensible by qiyas.
4
Examine the unspecified slave case
In the mahr example, an unspecified slave is owed. Since delivery of the exact slave is impossible due to unknown description, the husband may pay value. This is called 'qada shabih bi al-ada' – judgment resembling payment. The rule here is that when the original cannot be delivered, value becomes the effective equivalent.
This illustrates an exception: when inability to deliver the original arises, value substitutes.

کرنے کا ۔ وايضاً اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اس صورت میں عہد وسط واجب ہو گا جو کہ اصل ہے لیکن اس کا وسط ہونا قیمت پر موقوف ہے جس کی قیمت اعلی ہوگی وہ عبد ا علی ہو گا۔ درمیانی قیمت والا وسط اور ادنی قیمت والا ادنیٰ ہوگا اس لحاظ سے قیمت اصل بنتی ہے۔ کیونکہ تعیین عبد اسی قیمت پر موقوف ہے تو قیمت من وجہ اصل ہوئی۔ نقضاء ها پس قضا قیمہ
But at the time of divorce their value did not exist? Nay, despite the fact that at the time of exit they were not valuable, still their being made equivalent to property in the contract of khul' is correct. So it became known that the contract does not need their being valuable. The meanings of the contract become valuable. So the value of usufruct did not become due by necessity of the contract, yet despite that their value is established in the contract. So this is a proof that in themselves usufruct are valuable. We say their value: this is a response to what was said in the first proof that something not valuable does not become valuable upon entry of the contract; so this response is in the form of a denial. Rather, they become valuable in the contract itself, by mutual consent. This being valuable by consent in the contract is contrary to analogy, because only that can be valuable property which is subject to possession; when usufruct cannot be possessed rationally, it cannot be valuable property. So their being valuable in the contract by consent of the parties is contrary to analogy, so it cannot be analogized upon. It has two meanings: one is that to declare usufruct valuable in usurpation cannot be analogized to them being valuable in the contract, because their being valuable in the contract is contrary to analogy; analogy cannot be made on a non-analogical matter. The second meaning: that usufruct in usurpation cannot be treated as equivalent to property by analogy to them being equivalent to property in the contract. This second meaning itself refutes their claim. Their claim was that usufruct being equivalent to property in usurpation is correct because they are equivalent to property in the contract. According to the first meaning, analogizing their value in usurpation to their value in the contract is rejected. For this reason, because value in the contract is contrary to analogy, therefore analogizing value of usufruct in usurpation is not correct. This is a proof of the invalidity of analogy in the first meaning. And the distinguishing factor is consent; this is an analogy in the second meaning, i.e., analogizing the equation of usufruct with property in usurpation to the equation of usufruct with property in the contract of khul' – that between them consent is a difference. In the contract, consent of the parties exists; in usurpation it does not. This is a proof of the invalidity of analogy in the second meaning. "And the witness does not guarantee" etc. This is a branch. What was said that if a thing has no known equivalent, its judgment cannot be given without a text from the Lawgiver; this is a branch upon it. The case is: two witnesses testified before the judge that the legally competent guardian had pardoned the retaliation. The judge issued a verdict of pardon on the basis of this testimony. Then these witnesses retracted their testimony, saying we gave false and lying testimony. They do not guarantee anything. No guarantee will be incumbent upon them because exacting retaliation is a meaning that has no known equivalent, and property is not its equivalent in form because exacting retaliation is a meaning of giving life, because by it the evil of the killer is repelled; it was possible that due to enmity he might attempt to kill the heirs of the victim, and pursue the children of the victim, and in this survival, the victim also has a kind of life. And property does not contain this meaning; therefore property cannot be its equivalent in meaning either. And if a non-guardian killed the killer, then the right of the victim's guardian, which was exacting retaliation, he has wasted; so no guarantee will be imposed on that non-guardian either. Because the witnesses and the killer of the killer have wasted nothing of the guardian's except the exacting of retaliation, and exacting retaliation is a meaning that has no known equivalent; hence its guarantee by property is not possible. And the judgment resembling payment, like value. If a person appointed a slave other than a specific one – this is an example of judgment resembling payment. The case is: a person married and stipulated a slave as the right of the wife, and the slave is unspecified. Then he should pay its value. This is judgment resembling payment because its being a judgment is apparent, since he is not giving what was the original, he is giving value which is a substitute. In reality it is a judgment. However, because the original, i.e., the unspecified slave, is unknown in description, although known by genus, because he will be a man and a human, but the description of being of low or high quality is unknown, therefore he is unable to deliver the original due to its unknown description. So inability to deliver the original, which is handing over the slave, is established. So in this case his value becomes obligatory; so as if now value is the original. Because the original was in fact the slave, and known by genus, therefore the same original, i.e., the slave, is initially obligatory upon him. Therefore the husband has the option to give an average slave or its value; whatever he gives, the woman is forced to accept it; she has no option to refuse. And also, another reason is that in this case an average slave becomes obligatory, which is the original, but its being average is dependent on value. Whose value is higher, that slave is superior; medium value is middle; low value is low. In this respect, value becomes the original. Because determination of the slave is dependent on this value; thus value in some respects became the original. Therefore its judgment is judgment by value.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary discusses a fundamental legal principle: something whose exact equivalent (mithl ma'qul) is not known cannot be subject to monetary compensation without explicit textual authorization. The author first addresses the status of usufruct (manafi') in contracts like khul'. Although usufruct is not inherently valuable in the same way as corporeal property (because it cannot be physically possessed), the Hanafi school holds that through mutual consent in a contract, usufruct becomes valuable. This is an istihsan (juristic preference) that overrides qiyas (analogy). Consequently, this ruling cannot be extended by qiyas to other contexts, such as usurpation (ghasp), where consent is absent. The commentary then clarifies two possible interpretations of that principle. Next, it applies the same principle to a case of witness retraction in a qisas (retaliation) case. When witnesses retract their testimony that the guardian pardoned qisas, they are not liable for monetary compensation because the right of qisas is a 'meaning' (ma'na) that has no known equivalent in property. The underlying rationale is that qisas has a spiritual and social benefit (repelling evil, preserving life) that property cannot replicate. Finally, the commentary discusses a case of an unspecified slave given as mahr. Although the original obligation is the slave, inability to specify him due to unknown description leads to payment of value; this is called 'qada' shabih bi al-ada'' (judgment resembling payment). The husband may choose an average slave or its value, and the wife must accept. This illustrates that when the original cannot be delivered due to impossibility, value becomes the effective equivalent.

Key Terms
استیفاء قصاص (istifa' al-qisas): The act of exacting retribution for murder, considered a right that has no known equivalent in property.
مثل معقول (mithl ma'qul): A known equivalent; a standard by which something can be replaced or compensated in property.
قضاء شبيه بالإداء (qada shabih bi al-ada): A judgment that resembles payment; when the original obligation cannot be fulfilled, payment of value is considered as if it were the original.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are witnesses who retract their testimony in a qisas case not liable for monetary compensation according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they acted in good faith and retraction is allowed.
B) Because the right to qisas has no known equivalent in property.
C) Because the judge's verdict was already executed.
D) Because they were coerced into testifying.

Key Takeaway
A right that lacks a known equivalent (mithl ma'qul) cannot be compensated by property; this usul principle limits qiyas and is exemplified by the case of qisas and witnesses' retraction.
